Moreover, if menstrual blood leaks, it can create sores in the orifices, causing non-stop dripping; when damp heat combines, it may cause excessive menstruation; when blood stagnates internally, it leads to symptomatic masses.

All these varied symptoms stem from mere blood stagnation and depletion. However, blood stagnation can also have conditions of false heat, and blood depletion can likewise indicate false heat. Thus, severe cases can lead to amenorrhea (absence of menstruation). In terms of stagnation and depletion, mild cases will show menstrual irregularities, while solely considering deficiency and heat respectively.[50p]
For blood stagnation and menstrual blockage that should be resolved, the causes are dietary heat and toxins, or excessive anger causing condensation of blood and phlegm. One must use substances like rhubarb and related herbs to promote transformation, allowing old blood to dissipate and new blood to be generated. If vigorous energy depletes the blood due to overwork and worry, it is better to nourish gently and harmoniously. If there is also phlegm, fire, or damp heat present, it is essential to clear and cool these conditions. Cinnamon is often used as an adjunct because it promotes blood circulation when there is heat, but one must not take harsh drugs that harm the Yin. Regarding the theory of depleting Qi while enhancing blood, although it is essential in gynecology, blood is paired with Qi. When Qi is hot, the blood is hot; when Qi is cold, the blood is cold; when Qi rises, it rises; when Qi descends, it descends; when Qi circulates, it circulates; when Qi stagnates, it stagnates. If there is accumulated fire energy in the blood, one may use Xiao Feng San or Qi regulating powder, supplemented with aromatics, areca nut, and bitter orange peel to open the stagnation and move the Qi.[51p]
When the qi is disturbed, it must be regulated; when the qi is cold, it needs warmth; when the qi is weak, it should be replenished; this applies to both men and women. Indeed, when the yang is strong, the yin naturally grows; when the qi is depleted, the blood will also decrease. Can one solely exhaust their qi? Many scholars mistakenly follow Shuhe, who argues that strong blood leads to weak qi, not realizing that Shuhe discusses the liver and lung meridians, implying that the liver should be strong compared to the lungs; in truth, a balance of qi and blood is necessary for conception, hence the saying, "the two organs must be harmonized." Yet women often face bias, and their aspirations remain unfulfilled. They frequently experience pent-up emotions and anger; thus, Xiangfu is considered a miraculous herb for women. The classics state: when pathogenic qi is excessive, there is fullness; when the right qi is lacking, there is emptiness. Must one not understand this?

During menstruation, if one experiences wind and cold entering the body, it can lead to stagnation and clotted blood; a slight warming medicinal soup is recommended. If menstruation is accompanied by a sudden onset of cold and heat, resulting in a blockage, whether it is cold or heat, it is all referred to as heat entering the blood chamber; one can use Xiao Chai Hu Tang with Sheng Di Huang, or Huang Qin Shao Yao Tang with Sheng Di Huang.[52p]
When one suffers from cold due to eating cold food or being exposed to dampness, leading to the stagnation of blood, one should use Wujisan with Mahuang, Mudanpi, and Honghua. If emotional stress causes Qi stagnation, use Fenxin Qiyin with Qianghuo, Banxia, Sangpi, Qingpi, and add Chuanxiong, Dangui, Xiangfu, Ezhul, and Yanhusuo. If there is heat present, add Huangqin or use a minor modulation formula with Xiangfu pill.

For cases of abundant Qi and blood, when the meridians are obstructed, or phlegm is present, one can use Dan Dahuang Gao. Alternatively, juice from Verbena can be boiled down to a pill or roasted until charred. Decoction of Honghua and Danggui can be taken.

For internal injuries from diet, overexertion, or weakness of the spleen and stomach, wherein one feels fatigue, has fever, abdominal pain, and reduced appetite without producing blood, one should take Buzhong Yiqi Decoction with Chuanxiong, Shengdihuang, and Tianhuafen. If there is abdominal rumbling and absence of menstruation, the issue is in the stomach, which is weak and cannot produce Qi and blood; in that case, one should use Houpo (five qian), boiled with water on an empty stomach, or just take a decoction of Cangzhu.

For diarrhea with reduced appetite, use Shengyang Yiqi Decoction. If there is no diarrhea and still reduced appetite, use Erchen Decoction with Baizhu, Huangqi, Tongbian, Zhi Xiangfu, Danggui, Shaoyao, Mudanpi, Maidong, Hawthorn, and Malt. For issues related to food stagnation, add Ezhul and Zhike.

If damp phlegm occupies the blood sea and causes menstrual obstruction, use Dantang Decoction with Chuanxiong and Huanglian. Do not consume Dihuang as it clogs the diaphragm; if used, ginger juice should be stir-fried. Indeed, the words of Danxi should not be taken lightly.[53p]
Heat in the stomach causes thirst, and those who eat well may gradually lose weight. When fluids are dried by heat, those who feel thirsty should clear the heat from the stomach. One can use a combination of Siwu Decoction and Tiaoge Chushi Decoction, called Yuzhu Powder; or alternatively, use the Liangge Powder, known as Sanhe Powder. For mild cases, a combination of Xiaochaihu Decoction and Siwu Decoction, removing ginseng and Banxia, and adding Tianhuafen is recommended.

Those with a thin physique, dry mouth, and a tendency to crave rich foods could have phlegm-fire due to stagnation. If there is a sensation of heat, one may use Xiaoyao Powder combined with Huangqin, without mint, or Siwu Decoction with Tao Ren and Honghua, or even add the nourishing Yangrong Pill.

Generally, the passage of water is blocked. Overweight individuals tend to have weak qi and damp phlegm, while thin individuals usually have a fear of blood and possess heat.

Young people may experience significant blood loss, or following drunkenness may engage in sexual relations, leading to depletion of qi and damage to the liver, especially if menstrual flow decreases. Treatment methods for these conditions can be found in the "Neijing," specifically in the section on abdominal discussions.[54p]
Miscarriage and excessive childbirth harm the blood, or mistakenly taking medicines that induce sweating and purging may lead to diminished blood flow and lack of energy. In such cases, use the Shiquan Dabu decoction.

If menstruation becomes irregular, with diminishing blood flow leading to stagnation, this is referred to as "blood desiccation." The root cause is insufficient emotional balance, which prevents the spleen from properly digesting food, causing a deficiency in lung nourishment and stagnant energy. Additionally, the kidneys' water element becomes deficient, leading to further depletion of blood over time. Initially, symptoms may include intermittent dripping; if the spleen and stomach become significantly weakened, it may develop into diarrhea and bodily swelling. If left untreated, this can lead to serious conditions such as abdominal masses and tuberculosis.

In summary, if menstruation is obstructed, without the presence of excessive heat, phlegm, or qi stagnation, the situation is generally similar. Adjust treatments according to the symptoms and harmonize diet to ensure the smooth flow of blood and energy. If there is significant stagnation, remedies such as Honghua Danggui powder, Ziqi powder, Tongjing pills, or Daojing pills may be used. For those with deficiencies, simply using Danggui powder to promote circulation is essential; afterward, it is necessary to nourish the blood and enhance yin to ensure fluid circulation. If one neglects to nourish qi and blood, relying solely on toxic medications for forceful treatment will certainly lead to death.[55p]
To speak of the expected period, those whose nature is harmonious and whose blood is sufficient can conceive easily; a difference of one or two days is not harmful. In terms of color, the heart governs blood, and the yin follows the yang; thus, red is the correct color. Even if not exactly on time, those with the correct color can easily adjust.

If the period is delayed by three to five days, it indicates blood deficiency. In this case, take Si Wu Decoction with added ginseng, astragalus, white atractylodes, dried tangerine peel, and bulblet. For thin individuals with merely low blood, double the amount of angelica and rehmannia in the Si Wu Decoction, adding a small amount of peach kernel and safflower. For those who are overweight and have a lot of phlegm, add south star, fragrant atractylodes, talc, chuanxiong, angelica, and cyperus to Er Chen Decoction.

For those who have a slight color and harmony, use Si Wu Decoction. If there is dripping wanting to stop, with irritability and rapid pulse, use Si Wu Decoction without chuanxiong and rehmannia; replace with three times the amount of eupatorium leaf and a little licorice, and take Ten Flavor Cyperus Pill. If there is internal cold and blood stagnation, with little flow or a shortened period lasting five to six days or more, use Si Wu Decoction with peach kernel, safflower, peony root, and sunflower.

If the period comes several days early, it indicates heat in the blood. Use Si Wu Decoction with added qin and lian; overweight people should add phlegm remedies. If it comes ten or more days early, both blood and qi are heated; use Si Wu Decoction with added yellow qin, bupleurum, and cyperus; for overweight individuals, add Qinghai Cangsha Pill with yellow lian and white atractylodes.

If the flow is abundant or lasts several days, five or six days or more indicates internal heat dispersing the blood; use Si Wu Decoction with qin and atractylodes. If thin individuals have fire, take Guo Jing Pill. For those who are overweight and have phlegm, take Qinghai Cangsha Pill.

Periods may come early or late, in large or small amounts; there may be a month’s delay, or it may recur in a month. In such cases, take Dong Gui San, Adjusting Menstrual Powder, or Dan Dan Shen San.[56p]
At times it flows, at times it stops, dripping continuously; pain arises in the abdomen, indicating that cold and heat evils are lodged in the body, causing pain due to stagnation of blood. If there are symptoms of intermittent diarrhea, healing occurs after excretion. If there is rebellious qi below the navel, attacking the chest and causing the urge to vomit, use Peach Kernel Powder; alternatively, take three qian of Danggui and three qian of Jangqi, formed into honey pills. For pain in the waist and abdomen, use Niu Xi Powder. If there is a change between movement and stillness, with heart pain, use Shixiao Powder. When the menstrual flow comes and stops appropriately, alternating between cold and heat, first take Xiao Chai Hu Decoction with added Di Huang, then harmonize with Si Wu Decoction. For frequent menstruation, increase the amount of Shao Yao in Si Wu Decoction and add Huang Qi. For continuous menstruation, add Di Yu, Ejiao, and Jing Jie to Si Wu Decoction. If hot, double the amount of Huang Qi or take Gu Jing Wan.

Purple discharge indicates wind, black indicates severe heat, pale white indicates deficiency, or it may be mixed with phlegm and stagnant water.[57p]
Like smoke and dust, like leaking water from a roof, like the color of bean juice, or mixed with yellow and muddy, this signifies damp phlegm. If it forms lumps or pieces and the color remains unchanged, it indicates qi stagnation, possibly due to wind-cold invasion. If the color changes to purple or black, this indicates heat in the blood. Generally, for purple, use Si Wu Tang with Fang Feng, Bai Shi, and Jing Jie; for black, Si Wu Tang with Qín, Lián, and Xiang Fu; for pale white, use Guo Qiong Gui Tang with Ren Shen, Qi, Bai Shao, and Xiang Fu; if there is phlegm, use Er Chen Tang with Qiong and Gui; if like smoke and dust, use Er Chen Tang with Qin Jiao, Fang Feng, and Cang Zhu; if like bean juice, use Si Wu Tang with Qín and Lián; if it forms lumps, use Si Wu Tang with Xiang Fu, Yan Hu Suo, Zhi Ke, and Chen Pi. Commonly used remedies include Hu Po Tiao Jing Wan, Bai Zi Fu Gui Wan, and Mo Fu Wan. The menstrual cycle should proceed normally; only then can one have offspring. If accompanied by tidal pain which intensifies with coughing blood, sweating, vomiting, or diarrhea with tidal sweat, then the blood will be further depleted.[58p]
When there is effective vomiting, the energy rises; when there is diarrhea, the essence flows to the back; when there is pain, it is a sudden obstruction in the middle. Therefore, one must first eliminate the illness before nourishing the blood and regulating the menstrual cycle. Among the conditions of tidal fever and pain, these are particularly common among women. This is due to blood stasis accumulating in the bone marrow, which leads to bone steaming; blood stasis accumulating and stagnating in the middle, conflicting with the daily generation of new blood, results in pain; if the blood is insufficient to nourish the whole body, it causes steaming heat externally; if the blood is insufficient and enveloped by excessive fire, or combined with phlegm, qi, or food stagnation, as well as external cold pathogens, it results in pain.

Tidal fever can occur at times due to internal injuries or deficiency; if it occurs at all times, it is due to external influences or excess. For deficiency, one should use the Great Warming Decoction; for heat, use the Four Substance Decoction with additional Chai Hu and Qin Pi; for menstrual obstruction, use the Blood Nourishing Decoction; for bone steaming, the Great Hu Lian Pill or the Great Black Chicken Pill. For the five hearts tidal sensation, use the Four Substance Decoction with additional Huang Lian and Hu Huang Lian. If there is no sweating, use the Poria Heart Supplementing Decoction.[59p]
For those with sweating, use Xiao Yao San. For pre-menstrual heat, where there is blood deficiency and stagnation, add Mu Dan Pi, Tao Ren, and Yan Hu Suo to Xiao Yao San. For post-menstrual heat, where there is blood deficiency and heat, remove Chai Hu from Xiao Yao San and add Di Gu Pi, Sheng Di, Tong Pian, and stir-fried Huang Qin; this prescription can be adjusted to be an effective remedy for reducing heat.

For coughing, add Sang Bai Pi, Bei Mu, Jie Geng, Zhi Mu, and Mai Men Dong. For coughing up blood, add Sheng Di, Shan Zhi, and Mu Dan Pi. For vomiting, add Chen Pi, Ban Xia, and Xuan Fu Hua. For noisy stomach sounds, add ginger, stir-fried Huang Lian, or the combined formulas of Qing Lian with Er Chen Tang.

For common tidal fever, take Shen Qi Wan or Da Zao Wan, or use the ingredients of Si Wu Tang combined with one tael each of Tong Pian and stir-fried Huang Qin, along with one pound of Si Zhi Xiang Fu, formed into honey pills.

If there is abdominal cramping before a menstrual period due to blood stagnation, use the ingredients of Si Wu Tang, four qian. Add one tael each of Yan Hu Suo, Ku Lian, Mu Xiang, and Bing Lang.[60p]
For severe pain, use Wan Tong Wan. If there is pain when menstruation begins, it is due to qi stagnation; use Wu Yao Decoction. For qi stagnation and blood stasis, use Da Yan Hu Suo San, or the Four Substances Decoction with added peach kernel, safflower, curcuma, yan hu suo, cyperus, and wood fragrance; if there is fever, add Chai Hu and Qin Pi. If pain is intermittent before menstruation, it indicates blood excess; use the Four Substances Decoction with added yan hu suo, wood fragrance, coptis, and cyperus. For pain in the leg and abdomen, use Nei Bu Dang Gui Wan. If pain arises from the cold wind during menstruation, causing pain around the navel, it indicates cold qi invading the blood chamber; use Da Wen Jing Tang or Gui Zhi Tao Ren Tang. If pain occurs when menstruation is about to start, use the Four Substances Decoction with added chen pi, yan hu suo, peony root, and licorice. For pain after menstruation, it indicates blood deficiency; use Ba Wu Tang or Xiao Wu Ji Wan.[61p]
For many years, suffering from cold blood has resulted in blockages at the womb exit, causing vomiting of saliva, pain in the navel and sides, and coldness penetrating to the waist and spine. Treatment includes wine-boiled Dang Gui pills and a warming meridian decoction.

For pain before and after menstruation, one can use a combination of Jiao Jia Di Huang pills, Zi Yin Bai Bu pills, and Qi Zhi Xiang Fu pills.

Menstrual blood is a remnant of the meridians; when the Chong and Ren meridians are harmonized, blood flows down as it should. Worries and thoughts weaken the heart blood, leading to fiery heat and the blood not returning to the liver, impairing its capacity for storage and circulation. If the mother fails to nourish the child, the spleen lacks refinement, leading to reduced appetite. With less food intake, the lung’s metal element fails to receive nourishment, cutting off the source of water and life, resulting in irregular menstrual flow.

Those treating should know that the heart governs qi and blood; when heart qi is stagnant, it is essential to regulate heart blood, allowing it to flow through the heart channels. The spleen and stomach regulate the circulation of qi and blood; overexertion and diet issues damage internal qi, leading to insufficient blood flow. If it flows intermittently, treatments like Ping Wei San or Si Jun Zi Tang should be applied to nourish the spleen and stomach, restoring the generation and movement of qi and blood. This is a thorough method, addressing both the symptoms and root causes effectively.[62p]
On the Matters of Young Women

When a girl reaches fourteen, her vitality is strong, and her menstruation begins. It is not until she nears twenty that she should be matched in marriage, indicating the difficulty in cultivating feminine energy. Some may indulge in excessive salty, acidic, fried, and hot foods, leading to stagnation of qi and blood. For this, one can use Honghua Danggui San, Zihua San, or Dan Dahuang Gao. If a girl remains unmarried past the proper age or desires a man before she is of age, this can hurt her heart's blood, causing heating of the spleen and drying of the lungs and kidneys, which can result in difficult-to-treat ailments. It is advisable to use Siwu Decoction with Huangqin and Chaihu, or Xiaoyao San with fried Shan Zhi, Qian, and Lian to nourish the blood, cool the blood, and lower fire. Alternatively, Shenshen Qi Wan can be supplemented with Ziqin and Honghua to nourish yin; Bazi Ren Wan is also effective. For those who become angry, the Sijizheng Wan with Huangqin and Shengdi is recommended. For those who have been startled, Baodai Wan can be used. If menstruation is completely obstructed, Wosong San is suitable.[63p]

On the Affairs of Widows

Widows suffer from many sorrows: some cannot forget their husbands, some are unable to support their households, and some long for their descendants to prosper. Their hearts are often aflame with worry, like rich food causing phlegm and fire. Symptoms include discomfort from wind and fatigue, alternating chills and heat, red face, and restless heart. Sometimes, they sweat abnormally with a tense pulse, indicating the need to suppress the liver's yin. Treatments include Chaihu Suppressing Liver Decoction, Yin Suppressing Rehmannia Pills, and Yao Ju Pills. For those who are impoverished and have a bland diet, use the four preparations of Xiangfu. If one suffers from confusion in their mind each morning, fears light, and dislikes hearing voices, and only feels better after noon; along with symptoms like dizziness, abdominal pain, and anxiety, especially when menstruation approaches, these are signs indicating an inability to fulfill one’s desires. They should focus on calming the spirit and nourishing the body, using Si Wu Decoction with Ren Shen, Fu Shen, Chen Pi, Chai Hu, Qiang Huo, Gan Cao, and Xiangfu.

Parasitic Conditions and Menstrual Irregularities

A woman experiencing menstrual obstruction and abdominal enlargement within a month may face complications such as pain, indicating a parasitic condition, treatable with Ying Sha Pills or Wan Ying Pills.

Temperament and Menstrual Regularity

Women of a harmonious temperament tend to have regular menstruation; those who are jealous may experience irregular cycles.

Hidden and Obstructed Menstruation

When a woman's monthly flow is absent, it is also referred to as hidden and obstructed menstruation.[64p]
The Distinction of Male and Female in Vital Gate

Men store essence through this, while women tether their wombs. Men's essence is primarily influenced by Qi, with the Kan water in action, hence the steam becomes essence and appears white; in the presence of fire, it may also appear red. Women, on the other hand, are primarily governed by blood, with the Li fire in action, hence their blood fills and manifests as menstruation, appearing red; if phlegm is present, menstruation may appear white.

Distinction in Blood Chamber between Men and Women

In men's blood chambers, there is no accumulation and thus no fullness; in women's blood chambers, there is accumulation that overflows as menstruation.

Pulse Method

A floating pulse with a weak quality indicates fullness in the sides and leads to obstruction in menstruation. This refers to the liver pulse. Weakness in liver blood causes fullness in the sides, resulting in coagulated blood and obstructed menstruation. A floating, empty pulse harms essence and leads to amenorrhea. This refers to the kidney pulse. Seeing this pulse indicates loss of essence in men and menstrual irregularity or amenorrhea in women.

For menstrual disorders, the pulse is soft as usual. Although the pulse at the cun position is balanced, there is pain in the chi position. A deep, slow, and weak pulse indicates excess; a caution for many incoming issues. A slightly deficient pulse is unbeneficial; what harm is there in intervals between months? If the floating and sinking are equal and slightly late or weak, after three months, the Qi and blood are insufficient. After more than three months, amenorrhea becomes difficult to handle. If there are heart and spleen issues, the floating is absent at the cun position. If the heart is insufficient, the left cun feels firm and knotty.

In general, a woman's pulse is often more moist and weak than a man's. A pulse that feels normal, even if menstruation is earlier or later, whether it be more or less, or even absent for a month, does not constitute a menstruation disorder.[65p]
The pulse at the inch is normal, while the pulse at the cubit is absent or weak; if it does appear, it is faint. This indicates accumulation and pain in the lower abdomen and digestive system, with an urgent sensation in the heart, and the menstrual flow is not smooth. If the pulse is deep and slow, it suggests deficiency below, leading to abundant menstruation. If it is slightly weak and does not lead to sweating, the menstrual cycle will definitely come after two months, commonly referred to as a missed period. When the three positions fluctuate and one remains still, the inch pulse is slightly slippery, indicating a weak stomach qi, the slippery nature shows insufficient fluids and blood. If the cubit pulse is slightly weak and slow, it suggests a lack of fluids; retreating reveals cold within the yin, indicating retention in the cycle.

If the menstruation occurs once every three months, it may become scanty and not flow later, particularly for those who have experienced miscarriage or multiple births, this is referred to as blood exhaustion. The classic texts state that diseases of the two yang affect the heart and spleen, causing obstruction in their pathways, thus a woman misses her period. This occurs due to insufficient heart energy, leading to a lack of spleen function in digestion, causing the lung metal to lose nourishment, which cannot produce the needed fluid for the limbs, resulting in daily depletion of blood. Initially presenting with a profuse and untimely discharge; if the spleen and stomach are significantly weakened, this can turn into diarrhea with body swelling. If neglected, it can lead to serious conditions like tumors and consumption.

The kidney pulse is deep and slight, indicating qi deficiency; in women, this leads to irregular menstruation and band-like sensations.[66p]

Diagnosis and Inquiry of Menstrual Issues

Menstrual issues may indicate either blood heat or blood deficiency; or during menstruation, there may be external factors that cause the symptoms to dissipate after the cycle ends. One should not use medication recklessly, as it may lead to complications with the blood sea. If menstruation is absent, it may be accompanied by symptoms such as tidal fever, coughing, diarrhea, blood loss, or white discharge. If one can eat properly, the blood can be regulated, and the symptoms will resolve on their own. However, gradual loss of appetite and weight can be concerning.

Heat Entering the Blood Chamber Causes Chest Tightness

Zhongjing's writings on cold damage do not distinguish between genders, but for women, blood plays a central role. The blood chamber refers to the Chong meridian and blood sea. If there is fever from cold damage coinciding with the menstrual cycle such that it is clear during the day but leads to confusion or delirium at night, this is termed 'internal heat due to blood stagnation.' When menstruation ends, the heat subsides with the blood, and if untreated, it may heal on its own. However, if the heat diminishes and the body feels cool, yet there is a sensation of fullness in the chest like tightness, or if confusion continues, it indicates that pathogenic energy has settled in the chest and side. If palpation causes pain, this is also referred to as chest tightness due to blood stagnation, and remedies such as Hai Ge San or Gui Zhi Hong Hua Tang should be applied.

For women who suffer from cold damage with alternating chills and fever, and menstruation suddenly halts, this is termed 'heat entering the blood chamber,' which leads to stagnation of blood. In such cases, Xiao Chai Hu Tang or Huang Long Tang with additions of Mu Dan Pi and Tao Ren may be effective. This condition is primarily seen in women, and inducing sweating or purging should be avoided. If there is excessive joy or delirium, and abdominal distention is noted, it is advisable to use blood-letting techniques; however, one should not be constrained by the notion that menstruation must occur. Both genders have a blood sea, and if men experience heat in the blood chamber, it may lead to reckless behavior resulting in blood loss and confusion—observations marked by symptoms typical of the Yangming syndrome. Men are often affected through the Yangming, while women are influenced by their menstrual cycle.[67p]
On Moon Water

Women are of the yin category, with blood as their primary substance. Their blood responds to the moon, reflecting its phases, and corresponds with tidal movements—both the moon's waxing and waning and the tides' ebb and flow. The menstrual cycle occurs monthly, in harmony with the moon, hence it is called lunar trust, lunar water, and menstrual cycle. The term "cycle" signifies regularity and established patterns. The "heavenly essence" refers to the life-giving water of heaven. Some practitioners erroneously refer to this as "red lead," which is a misnomer.

A woman’s menstrual cycle occurs monthly as per her natural condition. Variations may arise, with issues such as delayed or obstructed flow indicating illness. Moreover, there are changes in regularity that ancient texts did not address and that should not be overlooked. Some may experience menstrual flow accompanied by spotting or bleeding from the eyes, which is referred to as irregular flow. Others may have a cycle every three months or may never cycle while conceiving, classified as "hidden menstruation." After conception, if a woman menstruates monthly and gives birth, this is termed a "prosperous fetus," commonly referred to as a "dirty fetus." If months pass with significant bleeding yet the fetus does not abort, it is considered a "leaky fetus." Although these situations pertain to the abundance or deficiency of qi and blood, they still deviate from the norm.

When a girl reaches the age of fourteen, her heavenly essence manifests, and at twenty-one, it ceases, which is typical. There are accounts of girls aged twelve or thirteen becoming pregnant, as recorded in "Records of the Chusan Family," noting a girl from Jiangsu who conceived at twelve. There are also instances of women in their fifties or sixties giving birth, as mentioned in the "History of Liao," where a woman over sixty bore two sons and a daughter, which is indeed an exceptional case.[68p]
Physicians should pay attention to this matter. When women menstruate, the foul, unpleasant fluids are dangerous, thus the noble should avoid them for their impurity, as they can harm the Yang and cause illness. Those who prepare decoctions for medicinal purposes, those who practice inoculation, and those who cultivate sexual harmony, all should refrain from such practices for this reason. The "Boweizhi" states that the country of Funan has a strange technique that prevents blades from cutting; if the blade is coated with menstruation water, it will perish. This is the foul fluid that harms the spirit, hence all medicinal substances should avoid contact with it. This claim is well supported. Nowadays, there are charlatans and sorcerers luring the foolish with tricks, using laws to obtain young maidens upon their first menstruation, calling it "primal red lead." They concoct names and recipes, linking it to the "Golden Flowers" of the "Certificate of Mutual Assurance," and the primary scripture of the "Wuzhen Pian," referring to the same thing. Foolish individuals believe them, consuming the foul residues thinking they possess secret formulas, often leading to the emergence of ailments, which is truly lamentable. Thus, Xiao Liao's poem on the true gold elixir states: "Those of the lower path have a nature inclined to indulgence, forcefully seeking to gather the Yang from others' Yin. Holding the heavenly essence in the mouth, it is called a remedy, yet it seems a futile effort." One can derive wisdom from this.

For women experiencing amenorrhea, there are signs of excess and deficiency. Excess indicates stagnant blood, while deficiency suggests liver injury. The "Su Wen" states: "When young, if there has been significant blood loss, or if one drunkenly enters a room, the Qi is exhausted and the liver harmed, hence the monthly cycle diminishes and may cease. Treat it with four fish bones and one Zhi jiao herb." This pertains to the sickness of blood blockage due to deficiency.[69p]
Comprehensive Collection of Ancient and Modern Books, Volume 382: Women's Meridian Section

Guidelines for Diagnosis and Treatment (Ming Dynasty, Wang Kentang)

On Menstrual Irregularities and Identification of Stagnant Blood

Zhongjing treats menstrual irregularities with abdominal fullness and pain. If the menstruation occurs again in a month, use the Earth Gourd Root Powder. This remedy is designed to break down stubborn blood stagnation, indicating that menstruation is delayed due to stagnant blood. This was not previously discussed. To identify stagnant blood, one must differentiate between fullness and pain in the lower abdomen.

Discussion on Dongyuan and Jiegugu's Method for Treating Blood Deficiency

Both Dongyuan and Jiegugu's methods for treating blood deficiency focus on nourishing the blood and clearing heat. To nourish blood, remedies like the Four Substance Decoction are used. For clearing heat, Dongyuan classifies the conditions into three regions: if heat is in the middle, it leads to good appetite with thirst; treatment involves regulating the stomach with substances like Chengqi. If heat is in the lower part, causing constipation, it is treated with substances like Yuzhu, which is equal parts of the Four Substances and Chengqi. If heat is in the upper area, resulting from overthinking, it is treated with herbs like Qín and Lián, along with Sanhe. Sanhe is a mixture of the Four Substances, Cool the Diaphragm, and Donggui. Jiegugu states that one should first take calming heart fire remedies, also including Qín, Lián, Sanhe, and Yuzhu; then, one should take five nourishing remedies for health, which also include energizing agents.[70p]
Menstrual Disorders

1. Purple and Black Flow

When the external pathogen first affects, there must be pain. If there is no pain, over time it will accumulate and transform into heat. Moreover, cold leads to stagnation, thus resulting in a purple-black flow; it is not due to cold.

2. Pain During Menstruation

Menstruation involves the movement of qi and blood, connecting yin and yang, and nourishing the body. When qi and blood are abundant and yin and yang are balanced, the body is unimpeded. However, if the protective qi is insufficient to nourish, and there is a lack of blood to irrigate internally, then when the qi and blood are insufficient, menstruation may come, leading to pain in the body first.

3. Delay Beyond Period

According to "Chuan Bao," a man born in the year of the Tiger belongs to wood, with yin present in yang, hence he obtains the number eight. A woman born in the year of the Monkey belongs to metal, with yang present in yin, hence she obtains the number seven. Men are governed by qi; once the eight is complete, the number is exhausted, and this leads to weakness in yang essence. Women are governed by blood; once the seven is complete, the number is finished, leading to cessation of menstruation. When the Chong meridian is vacuous and weak, if the celestial and earthly pathways are unconnected, then there will be no offspring. Sometimes, excessive labor or mismanagement of emotions, during the time when the meridians become weak, can result in attacks by pathogenic qi, causing menstruation to not stop and leading to flooding.[71p]
Women's Secret Medicine
Ming Dynasty - Wanquan

General Treatise

Yin and Yang are fundamentally different; men and women are of different categories. There are specialized treatments for different ailments, aimed at alleviating deep-seated illnesses in women. Menstruation arrives like the tides at its due time; the blood flow is ever-present, resembling the continuous waves of a river. When deemed without illness, one may forgo medicine. Yet, if it comes early before its time, the qi may be excessive and the blood can easily diminish; if it comes late, the qi may be insufficient, and the blood weak from the beginning. If the floral essence is faint, it indicates a deficiency in the blood's water; if the peach waves are purple, it shows the fire scorching the womb. If menstruation hasn’t occurred and there’s abdominal pain, it suggests qi stagnation and blood clumping which can be adjusted; if menstruation has occurred and there’s abdominal pain, it necessitates harmony in qi and nurturing the blood without errors.

Menstruating twice in a month indicates an invasion of fiery pathogens prompting qi and blood not to hold; menstruating once in several months results from depletion of original qi, leading to insufficient transformation. These are all signs of true deficiency, where balance and treatment are of utmost importance. Fullness without discharge means amenorrhea, blood desiccation, or the presence of masses; discharge without fullness signifies menorrhagia, leukorrhea, or profuse flow. Those who are consistently full dread the fullness within; those who frequently discharge worry about the loss of qi. The pulse loves to feel empty and weak, while diagnosis should avoid the excessive and rapid. Those who endure pain silently exacerbate their ailments; foolish women hasten their demise. Prematurely attacking with tonics may worsen the conditions; incompetent physicians may inadvertently worsen the afflictions.[72p]
General Discussion

According to the classics: when a girl reaches the age of fourteen, her menstruation begins, marking the onset of her reproductive capability. Hence, when the cycles are regular, it indicates good health, and one should not rashly use medicines to regulate the cycles. If menstruation occurs before or after the expected time, if it happens twice in ten months, if it appears only once over several months, if it ceases completely, if there is excessive bleeding, or if there are unusual discharges, all these conditions indicate a disruption of regular cycles and require adjustment.

Generally, the methods of treatment are as follows: if there is heat, clear it; if there is cold, warm it; if there is deficiency, tonify it; if there is stagnation, move it; if there is excess, solidify it; if there is descent, elevate it. Treatment should be administered based on the diagnosis, aiming for balance. For example, Qinghao, Lian, Zhi, and Bai are cooling herbs; ginger, cassia, Ding, and Fu are warming herbs; ginseng, Jizhu, Angelica, and Fu are tonifying herbs; Chuanxiong, Xiangfu, Qingpi, and Yanhusuo are herbs for moving stagnation; oyster, red stone fat, palm ash, and arborvitae leaves are for solidifying essence; and Shengma, Chaihu, Jingjie, and Baizhi are for elevating. When used according to the symptoms, effectiveness is rarely lacking.[73p]
There are three reasons for irregular menstrual cycles in women:

  1. Spleen deficiency
  2. Damage to the chong and ren vessels
  3. Phlegm and fat accumulation

In treating diseases, one must examine these conditions carefully. For those with weakened spleen and stomach: it is said that diseases of the two yang (the yangming and the stomach) manifest in the heart and spleen, leading to women not having their monthly cycles. The two yang refer to the yangming stomach, which is responsible for receiving and nourishing grains, fostering blood and qi, irrigating the organs, and facilitating circulation. It is the sea of food and the mother of blood and qi. However, worry and excessive thinking harm the heart. If the heart qi is damaged, the splenic qi cannot be nourished, leading to stagnation and blockage. Although the stomach can still receive food, it fails to perform its nourishing and irrigating functions, resulting in the loss of vital commands. Consequently, spleen and stomach deficiency leads to reduced appetite, gradual depletion of qi and blood, and conditions such as blood stagnation, pale complexion, delayed menstruation, and irregular cycles every few months.

As for damage to the chong and ren vessels: it is said that gathering and exhaling influences blood and its nourishment. Therefore, when qi flows, blood flows; when qi is stagnated, blood becomes stagnant as well.[74p]
The nature of women is obstinate and impulsive, prone to anger and jealousy, which harms the liver qi. The liver is the sea of blood; when the channels are obstructed, blood and qi will run awry. Moreover, Zhu states: If a woman's blood has not yet flowed but is forced, it can lead to misnamed ailments later on. Thus, if a man forcibly associates with a woman before she reaches the age of fourteen or during her menstrual period, it can cause internal injury leading to unregulated blood flow, and if this happens for two cycles, it can result in a miscarriage or leakage.

As for phlegm and fat accumulation, a woman's body should have open internal pathways, with no obstructions, while externally, the menstrual channels should flow smoothly, allowing for timely blood and qi. However, those who are overweight and full of fat have their foundational doors blocked, and if phlegm obstructs, the tides of the blood sea do not flow. Therefore, one may have delayed menstruation, experience minimal flow for several months, or suffer from abnormal discharges, menstrual obstructions, or infertility.[75p]
Preliminary Treatment Methods

If the person has a mild disposition and no other ailments, blame their abundant and heated blood. Use ingredients like Rehmannia, Chuanxiong, Red Peony, Fresh Rehmannia, Anemarrhena, Ophiopogon, Prepared Rehmannia, and Licorice. If the person is irritable, prone to anger and jealousy, blame the heat in both qi and blood, coupled with stagnation. Use Rehmannia, Chuanxiong, White Peony, Fresh Rehmannia, roasted Scutellaria, roasted Coptis, urine-preserved Cyperus, and similar ingredients. If the individual is thin and has no other diseases, blame their blood heat. Use Four Substances Decoction combined with roasted Scutellaria and Coptis, Red Peony, and Licorice, along with Sanbu Pills. If the individual is thin but has many diseases and heat, blame internal injuries in the Chong and Ren channels. Use Rehmannia, White Peony, Cooked Rehmannia, Ginseng, Anemarrhena, Ophiopogon, Chuanxiong, roasted Licorice, ginger, and jujube, and it is better to regularly take Rehmannia Pills. If they mistakenly took hot and spicy medications, blame the repressed fire in the Chong and Ren channels. Use Rehmannia, Chuanxiong, Red Peony, Fresh Rehmannia, Berberine, Anemarrhena, Akebia, and Licorice. If the person is overweight, has phlegm, and is prone to stagnation, blame their qi heat and blood deficiency. Use Rehmannia, Chuanxiong, ginger juice-preserved Fresh Rehmannia, half summer soaked in boiling water, White Poria, Licorice, roasted Scutellaria, urine-preserved Cyperus, roasted Coptis, and ginger.[76p]
Later Period Treatment Principles

If one's virtues are gentle and there are no diseases, the issue is attributed to insufficient qi and blood; use the Four Herbs and Four Noble Herbs, along with ginger and jujube. If one is impatient, easily angered, and jealous, the issue stems from reversed qi and insufficient blood; employ the Four Herbs and Four Noble Herbs with added green skin and fragrant substances soaked in young boy's urine, and regularly take Cangsha pills to adjust. If one is thin and has no other ailments, it is due to both qi and blood being insufficient; thus, use the Ten Complete Nourishing formula, along with ginger and jujube. If one is thin and eats little, it suggests a deficiency in the spleen and stomach, leading to weakened qi and little blood; use Yigong powder with Tanggui and Chuanxiong soup as the main treatment, and also take Dihuang pills. If one is overweight or consumes excessive food, the issue is due to damp phlegm stagnation and limbs feeling cold; use Liu Junzi with Guixiong soup as the main treatment, and also take Cangsha pills. If one typically has a lot of phlegm, the cause is a deficiency in the spleen and stomach, leading to poor nourishment of qi and blood; use Shenxiong Dabu pills and Dihuang pills. If one is impatient and frequently angry, the liver is injured, affecting the Chong and Ren vessels; use the Four Herbs with Chaihu soup as the main treatment, and also take Biyin pills to exhaust the fire from Chong and Ren. If one has previously taken warming and spicy medicines, use the Four Herbs with Huangbai and Zhimu soup alongside Sanbu Jiu as the main treatment. If there has been previous damage to the Chong and Ren vessels, use the Four Herbs, ginseng, Zhimu, and Maidong soup with Dihuang pills as the main treatment.[77p]
Treatment Methods for Several Months

For thin individuals, ascribe their condition to weak spleen and stomach, and deficiency of qi and blood; treat with Shiquan Dabu Decoction and Dihuang Pill. For overweight individuals, attribute their condition to phlegm accumulation and deficiency of qi and blood; treat with Liujunzi Decoction plus Cangsha and Phlegm-Expelling Pill.

Treatment Methods for Before or After

For conditions occurring before or after, address them as deficiency; adjust the Bazhen Decoction for treatment, and it is advisable to regularly take Black Chicken Pill.

Treatment Methods for Excessive or Insufficient Conditions[78p]
When a thin person has scant menstrual flow, it is attributed to deficiency of blood. The treatment is to use a decoction of Four Substances with added ginseng. In the case of a fat person with scant menstrual flow, it is due to phlegm and congestion in the meridians; the remedy should be a decoction of Two Elected Herbs with added chuanxiong and angelica. If there is excessive menstrual flow regardless of body type, it indicates heat in the body; the treatment should be a decoction of Four Substances with added scutellaria and honeysuckle, along with the Three Replenishing Pills. If the menstrual blood is purple, it signifies heat, and one should use a decoction of Four Substances with added cyperus and scutellaria. If the menstrual blood is pale, it indicates deficiency, and the remedy should be the Eight Substances Decoction, along with the frequent use of Rehmannia Pills. All the above methods of regulating the menstrual cycle should be applied during the time of expected menstruation, taking them continuously for more than ten doses, and the next cycle will be unfaltering. If using pills, they should be taken for a prolonged period for effectiveness.

There are three reasons for amenorrhea in women:

  1. When menstrual flow is absent due to damage to the spleen and stomach, leading to reduced appetite and depletion of qi and blood, the approach should be to nourish the spleen and stomach and replenish qi and blood, so that the qi can fill and promote the generation of blood, allowing menstruation to resume. One must not rashly use agents that promote menstruation, as this can further harm the central qi and dry up the yin blood, leading to diseases like tuberculosis that are beyond remedy.

  2. When menstrual flow does not occur due to emotional disturbances such as sadness, anxiety, anger, or resentment, which can cause qi stagnation and blood stasis, the treatment should focus on regulating stagnated qi and promoting the movement of blood, allowing menstruation to resume. Using tonics in this case would result in the qi being nourished but leading to further accumulation, and blood becoming more congealed, causing conditions like masses and abdominal distension.

  3. When there is a physical block due to excessive body fat, leading to stagnation of phlegm and fluids which prevents menstruation, the treatment should aim to regulate qi and resolve phlegm, thus allowing the menstrual flow to occur. This is what is known as skilled practice.[79p]

Treatment Methods for Spleen and Stomach Damage

For damage to the spleen and stomach, leading to insufficient blood flow, administer the modified Baizhong Yiqi Decoction. It is also advisable to take Shenzhushu Da Bu Wan and Wujirou Wan for relief according to the menstrual cycle.

Treatment Methods for Qi Stagnation

For stasis of qi leading to blood obstruction, the prescription is Kaibie Erchen Decoction. It is also advisable to take the Four-Ingredient Xiangfu Wan for relief according to the menstrual cycle.

Treatment Methods for Phlegm Stagnation

In cases of phlegm, use Cangsha Daotan Wan for treatment. It is also beneficial to take Kaibie Erchen Decoction with the removal of Atractylodes and adding Zhiqiao.

Treatment for Loss of Husband

For unmarried women who have missed their period, consorts who have lost favor, widows, or nuns in a convent, who wish to act but cannot, feeling anger without means to express it, and often suffering from amenorrhea; those who, out of shame, endure silently, which may lead to consumption and ultimately become irretrievable, should use the Four-Ingredient Xiangfu Wan and Shenzhushu Da Bu Wan. A combined approach of attacking and tonifying may provide hope for recovery. This transformation due to emotional imbalance is difficult to treat by standard methods.

Treatment Method for Weak Pulse

For amenorrhea, with symptoms of bone steaming and tidal heat along with a weak pulse, administer the modified Zengsuan Ba Wu Chaihu Decoction. If the heat is excessive and this does not improve conditions, add black dried ginger ash for effective results.[80p]
Treatment for Excess Pulse

For those experiencing amenorrhea with fever, dry throat, and dry lips, and an excess pulse, use the Four Substances Decoction and Cool the Diaphragm Powder as the main treatment.

Discussion on Regulating Menstruation with the Four Substances Decoction

For women with irregular menstrual cycles, the Four Substances Decoction serves as the primary formula, which may be adapted accordingly. This is because the true essence of the boundless, the refined energies of the two-fives, harmonize beautifully. The male is formed through the dry (yang) path, while the female is formed through the moist (yin) path. Women, operating under the moist path, necessitate a focus on yin when treating them. When the cycles of twenty-seven days come around and the celestial essence arrives, and menstruation occurs at the right time, women receive the yin energy from the moist path; within yin, there must also be yang. Thus, the cycle of menstruation is marked by seven: one seven signals the change of teeth, and two sevens indicate the arrival of the celestial essence.

Humans receive the energies of heaven and earth to live, thus they can be affected by these forces. The moon represents the yin of heaven; it waxes and wanes, which is why the blood of women also follows a thirty-day cycle, hence the term "monthly affair." The classic states that menstruation occurs on time, enabling conception. Therefore, for those with irregular cycles, this formula is appropriate as a base, allowing for adjustments based on cold, heat, deficiency, or excess. When the menstrual cycle is balanced, yin and yang harmonize, and all things flourish, leading to the ability to conceive.

The ingredients of this formula—Chuanxiong, Danggui, Shaoyao, and Dihuang—are all rich in essence. The richness corresponds to the deepest yin, thus they enhance blood. Analyzing further, Danggui is spicy and warm, invigorating the blood; Shaoyao is sour and cold, helping to astringe blood; while Shudihuang is sweet and moistening, capable of replenishing blood.[81p]
It is also said: Angelica is related to the heart and spleen, peony to the liver, and cooked rehmannia to the kidneys. As for Chuanxiong, it circulates the energy within the blood both upward and downward. These four substances are essential medicines for women, and for regulating menstruation, they must be used as the main ingredients. A rapid pulse with purple-black blood indicates internal heat; in this case, add Huangqin and Huanglian. A slow pulse with blood stagnation indicates cold; here, add Guangui and Fuzi. For those who are overweight with phlegm, add Banxia, Chenpi, and Nansheng. For those who are thin with fire, add Shanzhi, Huangbo, and Zhimu. For those with depression, add Xiangfu, Cangzhu, Sharen, and Shenqu. For those with stagnation, add Taoren, Honghua, Yanhusuo, and Rougui. A late period indicates heat, while an early period indicates cold, depression, air, or phlegm. For those with qi deficiency, add Ren and Qiyi; for those with excess qi, add Zhi and Pu. Someone might ask if there are circumstances where the four substances are not suitable. I would say: Yes, there are. If the breath is weak, Chuanxiong should not be used, as its pungent aroma could further disperse the genuine qi. If there is diarrhea, Angelica should not be used, as it is moist and slippery and could increase the downward flow. If the pulse is slow with abdominal pain, Peony should not be used, as it is sour and cold and could increase internal cold. If there is chest constriction, cooked rehmannia should not be used, as it is thick and greasy and could increase dampness. Those who understand will resolve these issues, while those who are ignorant will make mistakes.[82p]
The "Complete Book of Jingyue" by Zhang Jieben (Ming Dynasty)

The meridians are the essence of women.

The ancient Text on Natural Purity states: When a girl reaches the age of fourteen, the essence of her yin comes, the Ren meridian opens, and the Chong meridian is abundant, leading to the regular onset of menstruation, hence the ability to conceive. The essence of heaven refers to the postnatal yin energy; when the yin energy is sufficient and menstruation is regular, this is what is called the menstrual cycle. Because the female body is associated with yin, it responds to the moon, which waxes and wanes over three ten-day periods, while menstruation arrives regularly, hence it is referred to as the menstrual cycle or monthly trust. The term "cycle" means regularity; if there is any disruption, one loses their regular rhythm, leading to various ailments. Furthermore, since the cycle is fundamentally composed of yin blood, which is present in all organs, the blood from the organs converges in the Chong meridian, which is considered the reservoir of the blood of the five organs and six bowels. Therefore, the statement that when the Chong meridian is abundant, menstruation arrives on time shows that the Chong meridian is the essence of the menstrual cycle.[83p]
The transformation of blood and qi depends on food and hydration. When food and hydration are abundant, blood and qi are also abundant; when they diminish, blood and qi diminish as well. The sea of food and hydration is located in the Yangming region. According to the Treatise on Atrophy, Yangming is the sea of the five organs and six bowels, and it governs the nourishment of the connective tissues. The Chong vessel is the sea of the meridians, responsible for nourishing the streams and valleys, and it converges with Yangming at the connective tissues. The meeting of yin and yang at the connective tissues occurs at Qi Street, where Yangming dominates. Thus, both male essence and female blood descend from the front yin. It can be seen that the blood of the Chong vessel is entirely transformed from the food and hydration of Yangming, and the qi of the Yangming stomach is the foundation of the Chong vessel. Therefore, the essence of menstruation relies heavily on the Chong vessel, the stomach qi, and the heart and spleen; they are the source of generation and transformation. Other factors such as the seven emotions, six excesses, improper diet, and lifestyle discrepancies are nothing but thieves of heart, spleen, and stomach qi. One should discern what to pay attention to and what to eliminate, and learners should understand where to start from.[84p]
Causes of Diseases in the Meridians and Organs

Women are primarily governed by blood; when blood is abundant, the meridians are regulated, and offspring can be produced. The prosperity or decline of the body begins from this point. Therefore, in treating women's diseases, one must prioritize menstrual blood. In ancient medical texts, it is stated that the heart governs blood, the liver stores blood, and the spleen regulates blood; thus, any injury to the heart, spleen, or liver can result in meridian disorders. Furthermore, it is said that the kidneys are the deepest aspect of yin, governing closure, while the liver represents the more outward aspect of yin, governing the dispersal. Both organs possess a mutual fire that is associated with the heart; thus, when heart fire is disturbed, this mutual fire reacts, often leading to erratic blood flow. This is one explanation. However, erratic flow can also arise from excessive fire. If the central qi is deficient or if the gateways are unstable, erratic flow can occur as well, resulting from the deficiency of the spleen and kidneys, which cannot solely be attributed to fire. Additionally, if the qi pathway is obstructed and fails to move, this is due to liver stagnation. If the essence and blood are depleted and unable to move, this results from the exhaustion of true yin, with numerous associated symptoms that should not be mistakenly attributed to stagnation. Thus, these conditions clearly pertain to diseases of the heart, spleen, liver, and kidneys, while the lung is often less discussed; yet, one must recognize that the movement or stagnation of blood is invariably related to qi.[85p]
As the Classic Text states: When food enters the stomach, it nourishes and flows with qi, which is then transmitted to the spleen. The spleen's qi disperses the essence, which ascends to the lungs, connecting to the waterways and descending to the bladder. The essence of water is distributed throughout, and the five channels operate in harmony with the four seasons and the five elements, balancing yin and yang, establishing what is considered normal. This means that the process moves from the stomach to the spleen, then to the lungs, and subsequently spreads through the channels. Thus, if there is a departure of blood, one should replenish qi; if blood is stagnant, one should regulate qi. Qi is governed by the lungs, which is clear in its meaning. These matters reflect the necessary distinctions in the channels. However, if one examines the subtle intricacies, there are still further distinctions to be made. Generally, the onset of disease may stem from thoughts and worries, emotional stress, excessive labor, or the six evils linked to diet, often arising in the four organs of the heart, lungs, liver, and spleen; in severe cases, the four organs are affected, eventually implicating the spleen and kidneys. When yang is depleted, food intake decreases, leading to exhaustion of the spleen and stomach qi. When yin is depleted, essence and blood diminish daily, causing a decline in kidney qi. Therefore, I say: When yang pathogens invade, harm must return to yin; when the five organs are harmed, the consequence must reach the kidneys. This flow and source is inevitable, and is key to treatment. Consequently, when treating channel disorders, if the condition is not too severe, one should first resolve the underlying cause; if it has already become critical, one must consider the root and firmly secure it; to the point where both the spleen and kidneys are severely harmed, sources are depleting daily, leading to pallor and exhaustion, which could culminate in complete cessation. Those who mistakenly advocate simply breaking through stagnant blood will invite disaster swiftly. It is essential to avoid cold and cool medicines at any stage of channel activity, as well as in diet.[86p]
Menstrual irregularities

The menstrual blood is the essence of food and grains, harmonized and regulated in the five organs, dispersed and expressed in the six bowels, and can thus enter the meridians. Its source comes unceasingly, transformed by the spleen, governed by the heart, stored in the liver, disseminated by the lungs, and released by the kidneys, to nourish the entire body. In men, it transforms into sperm; in women, it manifests above as breast milk, and below it returns to the blood sea to form menstrual cycles. As long as the essence and blood are intact, emotions are balanced, diet is appropriate, the Yang generates, and Yin grows, then the meridians will be full, and what irregularities could there be? If one does not know moderation, the harm of the seven emotions is severe, followed by fatigue; perhaps also due to reckless desires, where strength and weakness conflict, leading to disharmony in the Chong and Ren meridians, these instances are not uncommon. Furthermore, external influences and internal injuries, or errors in medicine, may harm the nutritive energy, but there are always causes for such. People who are weak and often ill, unable to endure cold or heat, or wearied by labor, may often be those born with inherent frailties; however, if Qi and blood are properly nurtured but excessive indulgence leads to deterioration, or if the essence and blood are insufficiently full and are prematurely depleted, harming the source of transformation and growth, they will suffer lifelong consequences. This is the precursor to illness that should be thoroughly investigated and adjusted. If one wishes to regulate an existing condition, then the vital principles of deficiency and excess, Yin and Yang, are essential.[87p]
Danxi said: Those who arrive early face a heat in the blood; those who arrive late face a deficiency in the blood. Wang Ziheng said: If Yang is excessive, it arrives early; if Yin is insufficient, it arrives late. Variations in quantity, interruptions, and continuous flow are all due to the fluctuations of Yin and Yang, a major consequence of imbalance. However, if it arrives early, although there may be heat, if it is deficient and accompanied by heat, the focus should be on nourishing the essence and calming the blood. Moreover, there can be cases of arriving early without heat, which may require either tonifying the middle Qi or strengthening the vital gate, but one should avoid excessive coldness. Those who arrive late primarily belong to blood deficiency. However, there are instances where heat causes dryness and stagnation, necessitating a clear supplementation; if the blood reverses and remains stagnant, one must promote its flow. In general, the method of regulating menstruation aims for harmony, primarily relying on detailed assessment of the pulse and symptoms. If both the form and the Qi are abundant, it is permissible to use clearing and promoting methods. However, the manifestations of deficiency are often prevalent, while those of excess are rare. Therefore, the key to regulating menstruation lies in nourishing the spleen and stomach to support the source of blood, and nurturing kidney Qi to stabilize the residence of blood; this dual approach is ideal. If the essence is fundamentally deficient and one is unaware of nurturing it, it will inevitably decline and exhaust; this cannot be overlooked.[88p]
Distinguishing Blood Colors

In general, blood colors can be distinguished, and this naturally allows us to assess the presence or absence of conditions, and to identify cold and heat. If the blood is thick and abundant, this indicates robust blood; if the color is pale and scant, it signifies weak blood. This is a fundamental principle that is easy to understand.

Regarding the distinction between purple and black, the symptoms are as different as ice and charcoal, yet many people fail to comprehend this, leading to significant errors. Purple and black are closely related; nowadays, when people merely observe purple blood without distinguishing its true nature, they conclude it indicates severe internal heat. They fail to realize that bright red blood that is thick and forms patches or streaks is a sign of new blood in disorder, often resulting from internal heat. Conversely, blood that is purple and includes black, whether dispersed or thin, and that appears dark and stagnant, generally indicates a genuine depletion of vital energy and is likely associated with true cold.

If this condition worsens, it may resemble water leaking in a house or decaying old blood; these are all manifestations of purple-black changes. This reflects significant injury to the liver and spleen and a great decline of yang energy. In such cases, one should promptly use sweet warming remedies, such as Yin Jian, Li Zhong Tang, Gui Pi Tang, Si Wei Hui Yang Yin, and Bu Zhong Yi Qi Tang. If one solely focuses on tonifying the spleen, the weakened will be lifted, the exhausted will be secured, and one’s original energy will gradually recover, leading to the resolution of illness.

If one exclusively attributes the purple color to a heat condition, death will undoubtedly follow with the use of medicine. This applies equally to cases of bloody stools and related issues. Scholars must pay particular attention to this.[89p]
Blood Drought and Menstrual Closure

Blood drought and blood blockage are fundamentally different. Blockage refers to an obstruction; drought refers to depletion. Obstruction occurs due to the stagnation of pathogenic qi, causing the blood to reverse. Depletion arises from the deficiency of the Chong and Ren channels, interrupting the flow of blood. Generally, when women suffer illness for a period of several months, they invariably experience menstrual closure. This is because the yin has become depleted, leading to blood drought, where there is simply no blood.

Thus, whether due to weakness, fatigue, coughing, blood heat, reduced appetite, loss of blood, or any conditions without swelling, pain, or obstruction, if menstruation does not arrive for a long time, it is undoubtedly a case of blood drought and closure. To prevent it from drying up, nourishing the nutrients is essential; to unblock it, supplementing is crucial. Just as when snow melts, spring water flows naturally; when blood is abundant, menstrual pathways reopen.

When the source is abundant, who can obstruct it? Yet, the present-day practitioners ignore whether there is stagnation or not, often resorting to dispelling remedies, and in severe cases, exclusively using substances like peach kernel and safflower to facilitate flow. Do they not realize that stagnant blood can be unblocked, but dried blood cannot be? If blood is already dried, trying to unblock it will only exacerbate the condition, akin to squeezing out the last drop from a dried fruit! This shows a lack of understanding of the meaning of 'drought.’ This can cause significant harm; one should not fall into this error. The treatment approach should be combined with the previous principles of blood deficiency and kidney deficiency.[90p]
The text describes the condition of a maiden whose menstrual flow has not occurred for a long time. Zhang suggests that for a maiden experiencing prolonged amenorrhea, one must avoid using cooling herbs like qinghao. Many practitioners incorrectly assume that the maiden's blood is heated, and therefore apply cooling remedies. However, it is not understood that when blood is heated, it flows, and when it is cold, it congeals. The book "Essential Formulas for Health Preservation" elaborates on this idea, which is quite reasonable and should not be overlooked.

If the menstruation is slightly delayed and gradually stops, accompanied by pain in the limbs and weakness over time, along with a sensation of heat, and the pulse is weak and rapid, this indicates a deficiency of yin and weakness of blood, with excess yang prevailing. Insufficient fluid cannot diminish the rising fire, and the fire depletes the water, leading to the loss of bodily fluids. Treatment should focus on nourishing blood and yin, and one must be careful not to use toxic substances to force menstruation. It is advisable to use Baizi Ren Wan (a kind of herbal pill) and Ze Lan Decoction.[91p]
Blood Heat and Early Menstruation

Blood heat often arrives prematurely and must be assessed for its yin energy's strength or weakness. If the complexion is mostly red, or dark purple and thick, or there is excessive loss, the pulse will be rapid and smooth, with the internal organs desiring cold and fearing heat; all of these indicate types of fire.

To treat blood heat with fire, one should primarily use cooling and transformative herbs. If the fire is very strong, such as with herbs that withdraw heat, they may be used temporarily. However, one must not confuse false fire as true fire, or treat deficient fire as if it were excessive fire.

Generally, when heat is present, it tends to flow well, but if there's consistent early menstruation, herbs such as Xu Duan (Dipsacus), Di Yu (Sanguisorba), Dan Shen (Salvia), Qian Cao (Madder Root), or Zhi Zi (Gardenia) can all be employed. If there is a slight fire and yin deficiency leading to early menstruation, the treatment should nourish yin and clear fire, using decoctions like Bao Yin Jian.

Early menstruation should be considered approximately each month. Blood heat should be evaluated through the condition of the entire body’s organs. One should not hastily declare early menstruation due to imbalance when there is merely light bleeding. Neither should one classify it as heat solely based on the early arrival without evidence of fire in the pulse or symptoms.

If there is no fire in the pulse or symptoms, but early menstruation occurs, it indicates deficiency of heart and spleen qi, which cannot stabilize and retain the essence. In this case, one should use Da Ying Jian (Major Nutrient Decoction), Da Bu Yuan Jian (Major Original Nourishing Decoction), or a Five Blessings Decoction with additions like Du Zhong (Eucommia) and Wu Wei Zi (Schisandra) for treatment. These situations are quite common, and treating them as fire will certainly lead to mistakes.

If menstruation comes two to three times within a month, or arrives in as little as half a month or ten days, this indicates a chaotic state of blood and qi. Treatment should be adjusted based on the balance of cold and heat, and should not be treated merely as early menstruation.[92p]
Blood Heat with Early Menstruation

Those with blood heat often experience an early onset of menstruation. This occurs when the nutritive blood flows smoothly and is not severely depleted. If there is an internal yin fire eroding the blood, it may also lead to a delayed period due to the deficiency of water and the dryness of blood. The treatment should involve clearing heat and nourishing yin, using formulas like modified Si Wu Decoction, modified Yi Yin Decoction, or Eight Flavors Pill to nourish yin.

Blood Cold with Delayed Menstruation

Generally, those with blood cold will have their menstruation arrive later. What causes blood to be cold? It results from insufficient yang qi, leading to cold rising from within and causing a failure to regularize. This is what is often referred to as cold. When yin cold enters from the outside or internal cold injures, it could lead to blood reversal or pain; this is a different condition related to stagnation and should not be confused with blood cold causing delayed menstruation, which requires careful differentiation.

For those with insufficient yang qi and blood cold leading to delayed menstruation, the blood may appear dull, sometimes dark or stagnant and scarce. The pulse may be weak, thin, or deep, and the vital energy of the organs may manifest as aversion to cold and preference for warmth. These symptoms indicate a lack of fire in the body, and the treatment should involve warming and nourishing the blood qi, using formulas like Da Ying Decoction or Li Yin Decoction. Generally, since cold leads to stagnation, ingredients like ginger, cassia, Wu Zhu Yu, or Baijiu should be added, and in severe cases, Aconite should be included.[93p]
Blood Deficiency and Menstrual Irregularities

For women with blood deficiency, whether early or late, if the menstrual flow is irregular, one should examine the organ energies, discern yin and yang, carefully analyze the symptoms, pulse, and complexion, and prescribe accordingly to avoid mistakes. Generally, symptoms of blood deficiency may include a pale complexion, sparse flow, delayed menstruation, pain after menstruation where warmth and gentle pressure are preferred, fatigue following menstruation, weakness in the waist and knees, weak and thin pulses, reduced appetite, or a frail appearance. If there are menstrual irregularities accompanied by these deficiency signs, it is unwise to rashly apply depletive or cold treatments, as that may further damage the spleen and kidneys, worsening the situation. For cases of liver and spleen blood deficiency with mild stagnation and pain, the prescription of Si Wu Decoction is appropriate. One may also add cinnamon or scutellaria as needed based on hot or cold conditions, which is perfectly acceptable.[94p]
When the three yin are deficient and there is neither heat nor cold affecting the internal organs, small nourishment decoction, five blessings drink, and six substances decoction should be used; these are the most suitable remedies for ordinary people. Alternatively, eight treasures soup and ten complete tonics can also be selectively used.

When the three yin are deficient and there is also yang deficiency, large nourishment decoction and regulation of nourishment decoction should be utilized.

In cases of excessive worry and thought that have harmed the heart and spleen, seven blessings drink and return the spleen decoction should be prescribed.

If the spleen is not strong, leading to a reduction in appetite, and warmth and dryness are needed, warming the stomach drink and regulation of the center soup should be given.

For a spleen that is deficient and unable to control the qi, leading to leakage and frequency, five blessings drink, return the spleen decoction, longevity spleen decoction, secret source decoction, or four gentlemen’s decoction with chuanxiong should be chosen.

If the liver is unable to store blood, resulting in frequent shocks or urgent pain in the lower abdomen, three yin decoction and liver tonifying powder should be used.

If there is a deficiency of yin blood, leading to water not restraining fire and excess evildoer fire, resulting in night sweats, restlessness, or thirst and phlegm, this is a gradual decline towards consumption. Prompt regulation is necessary, using one, two, three, four, or five yin decoctions as appropriate; otherwise, there is a risk of blood drying out.[95p]
Kidney Deficiency and Menstrual Disorders

When women experience irregularities in their menstrual cycles due to desires in the bedroom, the underlying issue is often in the Kidney meridian. This condition is quite common and should be correctly diagnosed and treated.

If desires are unfulfilled, leading to prolonged thoughts and emotional distress, this may block the Heart and Spleen qi, causing depletion of the Kidney energy. This can either manifest early or late and may lead to gradual stagnation. In such cases, it is necessary to treat the Heart, Spleen, and Kidney, using remedies such as Xiaoyao decoction and Xiyuan soup.

If there is excessive fiery desire leading to the depletion of true Yin, it is advisable to use remedies like Baoyin decoction and the Eight Herbal Kidney Nourishing Pill.

If indulgence in the bedroom is reckless, it can certainly harm the movement of qi, leading to an inability of the Kidney energy to be sustained. Treatment should focus on strengthening the gateway of life, using remedies like Guyin decoction and Xiyuan soup.

If there is a deficiency of true Yin in the left Kidney and menstrual irregularities ensue, remedies such as Zuogui decoction, Zuogui pill, or Liuwei Dihuang pill should be employed.

If there is a deficiency of true Yin in the right Kidney and menstrual irregularities arise, one should use Yougui decoction, Yougui pill, or Bamei Dihuang pill.

If emotional distress causes illness, simply achieving emotional relief is crucial for efficacy. If the illness stems from indiscretion in intimate affairs, it is also difficult to rely solely on medicinal remedies without the willpower to exercise restraint.[96p]
Menstrual Abdominal Pain

Menstrual abdominal pain has both excess and deficiency conditions. The excess may be due to cold stagnation, blood stagnation, qi stagnation, or heat stagnation; the deficiency may arise from blood deficiency or qi deficiency. Generally, pain from excess often occurs before menstruation and lessens during menstruation. In contrast, pain from deficiency typically arises after menstruation has started, with pain persisting or even worsening as the blood is expelled. One can usually determine between excess and deficiency by palpation; pain that can be pressed and massaged is often deficient, while pain that resists pressure is generally excessive. It is important to recognize stagnation or lack thereof in these cases. However, there can be hidden deficiency within excess and hidden excess within deficiency; thus, one must consider both the physiological constitution and energy balance. Careful observation is necessary, as words cannot encompass all nuances.

For women experiencing pain due to qi counterflow during their menstrual period, particularly in cases of complete stagnation rather than deficiency, it is essential to promote qi flow and use herbal formulas to regulate the menstrual cycle. In severe cases, formulas such as those for expelling gas may be appropriate. If both qi and blood are stagnant, one can apply the formulation called "Lost Laughter Powder."[97p]
If there is cold stagnation during menstruation, it may be due to external cold disrupting the flow, or from habitual neglect of cold and chill, leading to a blockage and pain without deficiency. In this case, the cold must be expelled, and it is advisable to adjust the menstrual cycle with herbal drinks containing ginger, cinnamon, or dried immature citrus fruit, or to take a stomach-soothing formula cautiously.

If there is heat and dryness in the blood causing stagnation and pain, one should add ingredients to the Si Wu Decoction, or use a modified Baoyin Decoction with added or reduced herbs.

The above five symptoms should be examined for blockage without deficiency, as this is the true diagnosis. If there is a combination of deficiency, one must not forcefully intervene.

In general, women experiencing menstrual pain often have an element of deficiency; cases of pure excess are rare. One can distinguish between deficiency and excess by palpating before and after menstruation, which is a reliable method. However, some may have a fundamental deficiency in Qi and blood, resulting in poor blood flow.[98p]
When there is a refusal to press, there is often evidence before the period, indicating a deficiency of qi and stagnation of blood, leading to a lack of circulation. However, by examining the physical signs and pulse, for those experiencing pain due to weakness and insufficient qi, one should specifically use the Jue Jin Decoction or Wu Wu Decoction with modifications; their effectiveness is remarkable. Alternatively, formulas like Si Shen San may also be used.

If the pain occurs after the period, it is often due to blood deficiency, and one should use either the Da Xiao Ying Decoction with appropriate modifications or formulas like Si Wu or Ba Zhen, as they are also effective. It is essential to observe the cold, heat, deficiency, and solidity to serve as supportive measures, ensuring no lack of effectiveness. If there is residual stagnation, the Jue Jin Decoction is excellent.

For women who experience pain during their menstrual period, often accompanied by vomiting when eating, fatigue in the limbs, or combined with cold and heat, this indicates a chronic deficiency of qi and blood. In such cases, one should only use formulas like Ba Zhen Tang or Da Ying Decoction. For those with pronounced cold and deficiency, it is advisable to use the Li Yin Decoction gradually to strengthen and nourish, which will ultimately lead to recovery over time. If pain arises from excessive discharge and deficiency, the use of Da Xiao Ying Decoction should be adapted according to the state of cold and heat.[99p]
Heat Entering the Blood Chamber

When a woman suffers from typhoid fever or labor, or is affected by anger and heat, and then experiences her menstrual cycle, it can lead to heat entering the blood chamber. This may result in either unceasing bleeding or difficulty in blood circulation, causing her to be clear-headed and calm during the day, but to speak deliriously at night as if seeing ghosts.

If the heat comes from an external pathogen entering through the surface, it is advisable to use Xiao Chai Hu Decoction, or Three Chai Hu Decoction, or Four Chai Hu Decoction, or a well-known Huang Long Decoction adjusted with raw Rehmannia.
