If the spleen's energy is weakened and cannot control fluids, water will accumulate in the muscles, resulting in swelling. One should nourish bodily fluids and significantly support the spleen and stomach in order to maintain health.

(Note: Menstrual blood refers to the essence of yin blood and is related to the Chong and Ren meridians, producing milk above and menstrual flow below. Issues arise from spleen deficiency that prevents blood production, spleen stagnation that restricts blood flow, excess stomach heat that dissipates blood, deficiency of spleen and stomach leading to scant blood, emotional strain on the heart causing blood deficiency, liver damage from anger resulting in less blood, kidney water deficiency affecting liver blood production, and lung qi deficiency obstructing blood circulation.)[16p]

治疗之法，若脾虚而不行者，调而补之；脾郁而不行者，解而补之；胃火而不行者，清而补之；脾胃损而不行者，温而补之；劳伤心血而不行者，逸而补之；怒伤肝而不行者，和而补之；肺气虚而不行者，补脾胃；肾虚而不行者，补脾肺。经云：损其肺者益其气，损其心者调其荣卫，损其脾者调其饮食适其寒温，损其肝者缓其中，损其肾者益其精。皆当审而治之。】　　初虞世云：女子十四天癸至，任脉通，月事以时下，是有子。天癸者，物之自然。月者以月至，经者有常也。其来过与不及，皆谓之病。若荣血亏损，不能滋养百骸，则发落面黄，羸瘦燥热，燥气盛则金受邪，金受邪则为咳为嗽为肺痈为肺痿必矣。但助胃壮气，则荣血生而经自行。[17p]

The methods of treatment are as follows: if there is spleen deficiency and lack of movement, then adjust and support it; if there is spleen stagnation and lack of movement, then resolve and support it; if there is stomach fire and lack of movement, then clear and support it; if there is damage to the spleen and stomach and lack of movement, then warm and support it; if there is heart blood deficiency due to overwork and lack of movement, then rest and support it; if anger injures the liver and there is lack of movement, then harmonize and support it; if there is lung qi deficiency and lack of movement, then support the spleen and stomach; if there is kidney deficiency and lack of movement, then support the spleen and lungs. The classics say: "If the lung is damaged, nourish the qi; if the heart is damaged, regulate the defensive and nutritive qi; if the spleen is damaged, regulate diet and adapt to cold and heat; if the liver is damaged, alleviate the internal; if the kidney is damaged, nourish the essence." All must be carefully examined and treated.

It is initially suggested that when a girl reaches fourteen and has her first menstruation, the Ren vessel is open, and if menstruation occurs regularly, she is capable of bearing children. The first menstruation is a natural phenomenon. The monthly cycle has its regularity. Any abnormalities in its arrival or absence are considered a disease. If the nutritive blood is depleted and unable to nourish the tissues, it will lead to hair loss, a pale face, emaciation, and dryness; excessive dryness allows the metal element to be invaded, which can then manifest as cough, phlegm, lung abscess, or lung atrophy. However, by supporting the stomach and strengthening the qi, the nutritive blood can regenerate, and the menstruation will occur naturally.[17p]

须慎饮食，调七倩，保神气，庶可得生。若暴怒气逆，经闭不行，当用行气破血之剂。　　【注　按刘宗厚云：荣者水谷之精，和调于五脏，洒陈于六腑，乃能入于脉也。源源而来，生化于脾，总统于心，藏受于肝，宣布于肺，施泄于肾，灌溉一身。若阴气一伤，变证百出也。】　　夫冲任之脉，起于胞内，为经脉之海，手太阳小肠、手少阴心二经为表里，女子十四而天癸至，肾气全盛，冲任流通，经血既盈，应时而下，否则不通也。　　 【注　前证若禀阴血不足，用四物、参、苓；怒伤肝血，用加味逍遥散；郁结伤脾，用加味归脾汤；肝火怫郁，用加味小柴胡汤；胃经积热，加味清胃散。】　　寇宗奭曰：夫人之生。[18p]

One must be careful with diet, regulate the seven emotions, and preserve one's spirit in order to attain life. If one experiences violent anger leading to stagnation of qi and an absence of menstruation, one should use remedies that promote qi and break up blood stagnation.

According to Liu Zonghou: Essence derives from food and drink, harmonizing within the five zang organs, being distributed within the six fu organs, thus able to enter the meridians. It flows continuously, is transformed in the spleen, governed by the heart, stored in the liver, spread by the lungs, and discharged by the kidneys, nourishing the entire body. If the yin qi is harmed, numerous disorders will manifest.

The Chong and Ren meridians originate within the womb and are known as the sea of meridians. The hand taiyang small intestine and hand shaoyin heart meridians are closely related. A woman reaches puberty at fourteen with the arrival of Tian Gui, when kidney qi is at its fullest, the Chong and Ren flow freely, and menstrual blood is abundant and descends at the appropriate time; otherwise, there will be blockage.

If there is deficiency of yin blood, one should use Si Wu Tang, Ren Shen, and Ling; if anger damages liver blood, one should use Jia Wei Xiao Yao San; if stagnation harms the spleen, one should use Jia Wei Gui Pi Tang; if there is liver fire and stagnation, one should use Jia Wei Xiao Chai Hu Tang; if there is accumulated heat in the stomach meridian, one should use Jia Wei Qing Wei San.

Kou Zongshe states: The life of a person...[18p]

以气血为本。人之病，未有不先伤其气血者。若室女童男，积想在心，思虑过度，多致劳伤。男子则神色消散，女子则月水先闭。盖忧愁思虑则伤心而血逆竭，神色先散，月水先闭。且心病则不能养脾，故不嗜食；脾虚则金亏，故发嗽；肾水绝则木气不荣而四肢干痿，故多怒鬓发焦，筋骨痿。若五脏传遍则死。自能改心易志，用药扶持，庶可保生。切不可用青蒿、蝱虫等凉血行血，宜用柏子仁丸、泽兰汤益阴血制虚火之剂。　　【注　按经云：五谷入于胃，其糟粕津液宗气分为三隧，故宗气积于胸中，出于喉咙，以贯心肺而行呼吸。荣气者，泌其津液，注之于脉，化以为血，以荣四末，内养五脏六腑。若服苦寒之剂，伤胃必致不起。】[19p]

The foundation lies in qi and blood. When people are ill, they invariably first suffer a depletion of qi and blood. For young maidens and boys, excessive thoughts accumulate in the heart, leading to fatigue and harm. In men, this results in a waning spirit; in women, it causes a cessation of menstrual flow. Indeed, worry and overthinking damage the heart, causing blood to rebel and diminish, leading the spirit to scatter and menstrual flow to cease. Furthermore, a heart condition cannot nourish the spleen, hence loss of appetite; a weak spleen means impaired metal, causing cough; if kidney water is exhausted, wood energy cannot thrive, leading to dry and weak limbs, hence frequent anger, graying hair, and weak bones. Should the five organs be affected, death will follow. One can change their mind and resolve, and with medication to support health, one might preserve life. It is crucial not to use cooling blood-moving remedies such as Qinghao and Chuanjiao; it is better to use Baiziren Pill or Zexlan Decoction to nourish yin and blood and control false fire.

[Note: According to scripture, when the five grains enter the stomach, their dregs and fluids are divided into three channels, leading to qi accumulation in the chest, which exits through the throat, connecting the heart and lungs for respiration. Nourishing qi promotes the secretion of fluids which flow into the vessels, transforming into blood to nourish the extremities and internally sustain the five organs and six bowels. If one takes bitter and cold remedies, they will inevitably harm the stomach, leading to inability to recover.][19p]

　　　　　月水不利

　　妇人月水不利者，由劳伤气血，体虚而风冷客于胞内，伤于冲任之脉故也。若寸脉弦，关脉沉，是肝病也，兼主腹痛，孔窍生疮。尺脉滑，血气实，经络不利，或尺脉绝不至，兼主小腹引腰痛，气攻胸膈也。　　【注　前证属肝胆二经，盖肝胆相为表里，多因恚怒所伤。若本经风热用补肝散，血虚用四物加酸枣仁。若肾水不足用六味丸。】[20p]

Unfavorable Menstrual Water

If a woman experiences difficulties during her menstrual period, it is due to exhaustion harming her qi and blood, leaving her physique weak and cold winds invading her womb, which injures the channels of Chong and Ren. If the pulse at the inch is taut and the pulse at the Guan is deep, this indicates liver disease, which also primarily causes abdominal pain and sores in the orifices. If the pulse at the inch is slippery and the blood and qi are abundant, it suggests obstruction in the meridians; if the pulse at the inch is absent, it may indicate pain in the lower abdomen radiating to the waist and may cause qi to attack the chest diaphragm.

Note: The above symptoms belong to the liver and gallbladder meridians, which are interrelated. They are often caused by emotional distress. If due to wind-heat, use a nourishing liver powder; if due to blood deficiency, supplement with Four Substance Decoction plus sour jujube seeds. If kidney water is insufficient, use the Six-Flavor Pill.[20p]

　　　　　行经腹痛

　　妇人经来腹痛，由风冷客于胞络冲任，或伤手太阳少阴经，用温经汤、桂枝桃仁汤。若忧思气郁而血滞，用桂枝桃仁汤、地黄通经丸。若血结而成块，用万病丸。　　【注　前证若风寒伤脾者，六君加炮姜；思虑伤血者，四物加参、朮；思虑伤气者，归脾加柴、栀；郁怒伤血者，归脾逍遥兼服。若肝经怒气，甩加味逍遥散。若肝经血虚，用四物、参、朮、柴胡、牡丹皮。若肝经血热，用四物、牡丹皮。若肝肾虚火，用六味地黄丸。若肝脾血虚，用八珍加牡丹皮。若肝脾郁怒，用加味归脾汤。若气虚血弱，用补中益气汤。若脾不能摄血，用六君子加川芎、当归。若肝虚不能藏血，用补肝散。】[21p]

        Menstrual Abdominal Pain

When a woman experiences abdominal pain during her menstruation, it may be due to cold wind invading the channels and collaterals, or it may injure the hand, taiyang, or shaoyin meridians. Use Warm Channel Decoction or Cinnamon Twig and Peach Kernel Decoction. If the pain is caused by worry and stagnant qi leading to blood stasis, use Cinnamon Twig and Peach Kernel Decoction or Rehmannia Decoction to promote menstruation. If there are blood clots, use the All-Disease Pill.

[Note: If the previous condition is due to wind-cold damaging the spleen, add roasted ginger to Six Gentleman Decoction; if worry damages blood, add ginseng and atractylodes to Four Substance Decoction; if worry damages qi, use Guipitang with Chaihu and Gardenia; if anger damages blood, take Guipitang with Xie Yao. If liver qi is affected by anger, add Wei Xie Yao San. If liver blood is deficient, use Four Substance Decoction with ginseng, atractylodes, Chaihu, and Peony. If liver blood is heat, use Four Substance Decoction with Peony. If there is deficiency fire in the liver and kidney, use Six Flavor Rehmannia Pill. If both liver and spleen blood are deficient, use Eight Treasures Decoction with Peony. If liver and spleen are affected by anger, use the modified Guipitang. If qi is deficient and blood weak, use Tonify the Middle and Benefit Qi Decoction. If the spleen cannot contain blood, add Chuanxiong and Dong Quai to Six Gentleman Decoction. If the liver is deficient and cannot store blood, use Liver Tonifying Powder.][21p]

　　　　　月水不断

　　妇人月水不断，淋沥腹痛，或因劳损气血而伤冲任，或因经行而合阴阳，以致外邪客于胞内、滞于血海故也。但调养元气而病邪自愈，若攻其邪则元气反伤矣。　　【注　前证若郁结伤脾，用归脾汤；恚怒伤肝，逍遥散；肝火妄动，加味四物汤；脾气虚弱，六君子汤；元气下陷，补中益气汤；热伤元气，前汤加五味、麦冬、炒黑黄蘗。】
　　　　　天癸过期

　　许学士云：妇人经脉过期不及，腰腹疼病，成七七数尽而月经下者，宜用当归散治之。　　【注　前证若肝肾虚热，用当归散；肝血虚热，四物加柴、栀、丹皮；肝火内动，小柴胡加山栀、丹皮；肝火血燥，加味逍遥散；脾经郁火，加味归脾汤；肝脾郁火，归脾、逍遥兼服；肝肾亏损，归脾、六味兼服。】[22p]

Continuous Menstrual Flow

A woman experiencing continuous menstrual flow has abdominal pain that may be caused either by injury to the Qi and blood from overexertion or by the harmonization of Yin and Yang due to menstruation, leading to external pathogens invading the womb and stagnating in the blood sea. However, nurturing the vital Qi can lead to the self-healing of the illness; attacking the pathogen may instead harm the vital Qi.

[Note: If there are signs of stagnation harming the spleen, use Gui Pi Decoction; if anger has harmed the liver, use Xiao Yao San; if there is excessive liver fire, add medicinal herbs to Si Wu Decoction; for weak spleen Qi, use Liu Jun Zi Decoction; if vital Qi has descended, use Bu Zhong Yi Qi Decoction; if heat has harmed vital Qi, the previous decoction should be supplemented with Wu Wei, Mai Dong, and roasted Huang Lian.]

Menstrual Cycle Exceeding Its Regular Time

Scholar Xu states: If a woman’s menstrual cycle exceeds its time and she has pain in the lower back and abdomen, leading to menstruation after a full cycle has passed, it is advisable to use Dang Gui San for treatment.

[Note: If the condition is due to deficiency heat in the liver and kidneys, use Dang Gui San; if there is deficiency heat in the liver blood, modify Si Wu Decoction by adding Chai Hu, Zhi Zi, and Dan Pi; if there’s internal stirring of liver fire, modify Xiao Chai Hu Decoction by adding Shan Zhi and Dan Pi; if there is dryness from blood heat, add to Xiao Yao San; if spleen channel fire is blocked, modify Gui Pi Decoction; if both liver and spleen are afflicted by blocking fire, combine Gui Pi and Xiao Yao; if there’s depletion in the liver and kidneys, combine Gui Pi and Liu Wei.][22p]

　　　　　血枯

　　腹中论曰：有病胸胁支满，妨于食，病至则先闻腥臊臭，出清液，四肢惰，目眩，时时前后血，病名曰血枯。此年少时因大脱血，或醉而入房，亏损肾肝。盖肝藏血，受天一之气以为滋荣，其经上贯膈，布胁肋。若脱血失精，肝气已伤，肝血枯涸不荣而胸胁满，妨于食则肝病传脾而闻腥臊臭，出清液。若以肝病而肺乘之，则唾血，四肢惰，目眩，时时前后血出，皆肝病血伤之证也。　　【注　前证若饮食起居失宜，而脾胃虚损，当滋化源而佐以鰞鲗丸等药。若因脾土虚寒而不能生血，宜补命门火。若服燥药，郁火内作而津液消烁，宜清热养血。若脾胃亏损而气血虚，宜补中益气。若胃热消中而血液耗损，宜清脾胃之火。若大便秘濇，小便清利而经不行，宜清胞络之火。若劳伤心火，血涸而经不行，宜补心养血。】[23p]

Blood Depletion

According to the discussion in the abdomen: There is a condition characterized by illness in the chest and flanks, causing fullness that hinders eating. When the illness advances, one first detects a fishy and foul odor, produces clear fluids, feels sluggish in the limbs, experiences dizziness, and has blood that intermittently flows from both front and back. This condition is termed "blood depletion." It commonly occurs in youth due to significant blood loss, or from intoxication while engaging in sexual activity, which depletes the kidney and liver. The liver stores blood and receives ethereal nourishment from heaven, connecting through channels to the diaphragm and spreading to the flanks and ribs. If blood is lost and essence is depleted, the liver energy is damaged, leading to the liver's blood becoming arid and failing to nourish, resulting in fullness in the chest and flanks that hampers eating, thus producing the aforementioned fishy odor and clear fluids. If liver disease affects the lungs, one may cough up blood, feel fatigued in the limbs, experience dizziness, and see intermittent blood flow, all signs of liver pathology and blood depletion.

Notes: If the previous symptoms arise due to improper diet or living habits leading to a weakened spleen and stomach, one should nourish the source of transformation and supplement with medications such as fish maw and other tonics. If the spleen is deficient and cold, preventing blood generation, it is advisable to bolster the fire of the life gate. Should one take drying medicines that generate internal heat and consume body fluids, it is essential to clear heat and nourish blood. If the spleen and stomach are deficient and energy and blood are weak, one should tonify the center and benefit energy. If the stomach is overheated, leading to blood depletion, it is essential to clear heat from the spleen and stomach. For issues with constipation or if urine is clear and smooth yet menstruation is absent, one should clear the fire in the meridians. If exertion has harmed the heart fire, causing dehydration of blood and absent menstruation, it is advisable to nourish the heart and replenish blood.[23p]

　　　　　热入血室

　　妇人伤寒伤风发热，经水适来，昼则安静，暮则讝语，有如疟状，此为热入血室，治者无犯胃气及上二焦，宜服小柴胡汤。若脉迟身凉，当剌期门穴，下针病人五吸，停针良久，徐徐出针。凡针期门穴，必泻勿补，肥人二寸，瘦人寸半也。　　【注　前证若因劳役，或怒气发热，适遇经行而患前证者，亦用小柴胡加生地黄治之。血虚用四物加柴胡。若病既愈而热未已，或元气素弱，并用补中益气汤。脾气素郁，用济生归脾汤。血气素虚，用十全大补汤。】[24p]

Heat Entering the Blood Chamber

When a woman suffers from cold and fever during her menstrual cycle, if she is calm during the day and speaks confusedly in the evening, resembling a pattern of malaria, this is due to heat entering the blood chamber. The treatment should not disturb the stomach's qi or the upper two jiaos and it is advisable to take Xiao Chai Hu Decoction. If the pulse is slow and the body feels cool, one should needle the Qimen point, have the patient take five breaths, leave the needle in for a long while, and then slowly withdraw it. When needling the Qimen point, one must drain rather than tonify; for overweight individuals, needle two inches deep, and for those who are thin, one and a half inches deep.

[Note: If the above symptoms are caused by overexertion or anger that leads to fever coinciding with menstruation, Xiao Chai Hu Decoction plus Sheng Di Huang should be used. For blood deficiency, combine Si Wu Tang with Chai Hu. If the illness has already resolved but heat persists, or if the original qi is weak, use Bu Zhong Yi Qi Tang. For spleen qi stagnation, employ Ji Sheng Gui Pi Tang. For deficiency of both blood and qi, use Shi Quan Da Bu Tang.][24p]

　　　　河间六书 【金　刘完素】

　　　　　月水不调论治

　　妇人月水，一月一来如期，谓之月信。其不来则风热伤于经血，故血在内不通；或内受邪热，脾胃虚损，不能饮食，食既不充，荣卫凝濇，肌肤黄燥，面不光泽；或大肠虚变为下痢，流入关元，致绝子嗣。　　童幼天癸未行，皆属少阴；天癸既行，皆从厥阴论之；天癸已绝，乃属太阴经也。　　妇人气充经脉，月事频并，脐下痛，宜芍药六合扬。【一本是气冲。】 若经水过多，别无余证，四物内加黄苓、白朮各一两。若经事欲行，脐腹绞痛，宜服八物汤。若经水暴多，四物四两，加黄芩一两。若经水如黑豆水，四物加黄连、黄芩各一两。若妇人经水少而血色和者，四物四两，如熟地、当归各一两。[25p]

Discussion on Menstrual Disorders

Women's menstrual flow occurs regularly once a month, known as the "monthly sign." If it fails to come, it is due to wind and heat damaging the menstrual blood, causing it to become stagnant; or it may be affected by internal heat, with weakness in the spleen and stomach leading to inability to consume food. Without sufficient nourishment, the vital energy coalesces, resulting in a dry, yellowish skin without luster. Alternatively, if there is weakness in the intestines, it may lead to diarrhea that drains vital essence, causing infertility.

For young girls whose first menses have not yet begun, they belong to the Lesser Yin. Once the menses have commenced, they fall under the discussion of the Greater Yin; and if the menses cease, they belong to the Taiyin channel.

When a woman’s energy fills the meridians, if her menstruation is frequent and accompanied by pain below the navel, it is advisable to use a combination of peony and six ingredients. If menstrual flow is excessive without other symptoms, add one tael each of Huangqin and Baizhu to the Four Substance Decoction. If menstruation is coming on, accompanied by cramping pain in the abdomen, the Eight Substance Decoction should be taken. If the menstrual flow is significantly heavy, use four taels of the Four Substance Decoction and add one tael of Huangqin. If the blood resembles black bean broth, add one tael each of Huanglian and Huangqin to the Four Substance Decoction. If a woman has scanty menstrual flow but the blood color is healthy, use four taels of the Four Substance Decoction, with one tael each of Shudihuang and Danggui.[25p]

　　　　　血枯经闭

　　年少醉入房室，气竭肝伤，故经衰少不来。肝伤则血涸，脾胃相传，大脱其血，目眩心烦，故月事不来也，乌鱼骨圆主之。
　　　　　经水适来适断

　　妇人经水，通来适断，往来寒热，先服小柴胡以去其寒热，后以四物汤调治之。如寒热不退，勿服四物，是谓变证，表邪犹存，不能效也。
　　　　明理论 【金　成无己】

　　　　　热入血室

　　伤寒热入血室，何以明之？室者，屋室也，谓可以停止之处。人身之血室者，荣血停止之所，经脉留会之处，即冲脉是也。冲脉者，奇经八脉之一脉也，起于肾下，出于气冲，并足阳明经夹脐上行至胸中而散，为十二经脉之海。王冰曰：冲为血海。言诸经之血朝会于此，男子则运行生精，女子则上为乳汁，下为月水。《内经》曰：任脉通，冲脉盛，月事以时下者是也。王冰曰：阴静海满而去血，谓冲脉盛为海满也。即是观之，冲是血室，可以知矣。[26p]

Blood Exhaustion and Menstrual Cessation

In youth, intoxication leads to the bedroom, causing exhaustion of energy and injury to the liver, thus menstruation diminishes and does not arrive. Injury to the liver leads to the drying up of blood, and the spleen and stomach cannot transmit it properly, resulting in a significant loss of blood. This causes dizziness and heart restlessness, which is why menstruation does not come; it is manifested by the roundness of the black fishbone.

Menstrual Flow Appropriately Arrives and Stops

For women, menstrual flow should come and go appropriately. If there are signs of cold and heat, first take Xiao Chai Hu to dispel that cold and heat, and then use Si Wu Tang for adjustment and treatment. If the cold and heat do not recede, do not take Si Wu Tang; this is termed a transformation of symptoms, indicating that the exterior pathogenic factor still exists and cannot be effective.

Clarifying Theories

Heat Enters the Blood Chamber

In cases of warm disease when heat enters the blood chamber, how can we clarify this? The "chamber" refers to a place of confinement. The blood chamber in the human body is where the nourishing blood resides and is the place where the meridians converge, namely the Chong Meridian. The Chong Meridian is one of the Eight Extraordinary Meridians, originating from below the kidneys, emerging at Qichong, and along the Yangming channel, it ascends to the chest and disperses, becoming the sea of the twelve meridians. Wang Bing states: "Chong is the sea of blood," meaning that the blood of all the meridians converges here. In men, it facilitates the circulation of essence, whereas in women, it produces milk above and menstruation below. The "Inner Canon" states: "When the Ren Meridian is open and the Chong Meridian is abundant, menstruation occurs at the appropriate time." Wang Bing explains: "Yin calms, the sea is full, and blood departs," indicating that the abundance of the Chong Meridian means that the sea is full. From this observation, we can understand that the Chong is indeed the blood chamber.[26p]

伤寒之邪，妇人则随经而入，男子由阳明而传，以冲之脉与少阴之络起于肾，女子感邪，太阳随经便得而入冲之经并足阳明，男子阳明内热，方得而入也。冲之得热，血必妄行，在男子则下血讝语，在妇人则月水适来。阳明病下血讝语，此为热入血室者，斯盖并言男子，不止为妇人而言也。妇人伤寒，经水适来与经水适断者，皆以经气所虚，宫室不闭，邪得乘虚而入。《针经》有言曰：邪气不得其虚，不能独伤人者是矣。妇人热入血室，有须治而愈者，有不须治而愈者，又各不同也。[27p]

In cases of cold damage (shanghan), for women it enters along the meridians, while for men it is transmitted from the Yangming. The influences affect the Chong vessel and the Shaoyin network originating from the kidneys. When women are affected by evil, it enters through the Taiyang meridian and directly into the Chong meridian and the Yangming of the legs. For men, internal heat of the Yangming allows the evil to enter. When the Chong vessel absorbs heat, blood must move erratically; for men, this manifests as blood leading to verbal disturbances, while for women, it corresponds with the menstrual flow. When men experience Yangming illness with blood leading to verbal disturbances, it indicates heat has entered the blood chamber; this applies broadly to men, not just to women. In women, when the cold damage occurs, if the menstrual flow comes or stops, it is due to the depletion of menstrual energy; the uterus is not closed off, allowing the evil to exploit this entry. The "Divination of Acupuncture" states: "When the evil qi does not find an opening, it cannot harm a person alone." For women, when heat enters the blood chamber, some may require treatment for recovery, while others may recover without treatment; each case is different.[27p]

妇人中风，发热恶寒，经水适来，得之七八日，热除而脉迟，身凉和，胸胁下满如结胸状，讝语者，此为热入血室，当刺期门，随其实而泻之；与其妇人中风七八日，续得寒热，发作有时，经水适断者，此为热入血室，其血必结，故使如疟状，发作有时，小柴胡汤主之。二者是须治而愈者也。妇人伤寒发热，经水适来，昼则明了，暮则讝语，如见鬼状者，此为热入血室，无犯胃气及上二焦，必自愈，是不须治而愈者也。讝语为病邪之甚者，何不须治而愈耶？且胸胁满如结胸，讝语，是邪气留结于胸胁而不去者，必剌期门，随其实而泻之。[28p]

A woman afflicted with wind has a fever and feels chills. She experiences menstrual flow, which lasts for seven or eight days. Once the heat subsides, her pulse becomes slow, her body cools and stabilizes, but she feels fullness in the chest and sides, resembling a condition of constrained chest. If she speaks nonsensically, this indicates heat has entered the blood chamber. One should puncture the Qimen point and drain accordingly.

If the woman has been struck by wind for seven or eight days and experiences alternating chills and fever, with her menstrual flow abruptly stopping, this again indicates heat entering the blood chamber, and it is likely that the blood has begun to congeal, presenting a pattern similar to malaria with intermittent occurrences. In this case, Xiao Chai Hu Decoction is the principal remedy. Both of these conditions must be treated to ensure recovery.

If a woman suffers from a cold that causes fever, coinciding with her menstrual period, her mind remains clear during the day but becomes confused at night, resembling someone seeing a ghost, it indicates that heat has also entered the blood chamber. However, if this does not affect the stomach's energy or the upper two burners, she will certainly recover on her own; this does not require treatment to lead to recovery.

As for nonsensical speech, it indicates a serious presence of illness. Why is treatment not required for recovery in this case? Moreover, the chest and sides feeling full, akin to a constrained chest, along with nonsensical speech, suggest that pathogenic energy is trapped within the chest and sides, thus requiring the puncture of Qimen to drain accordingly.[28p]

寒热如疟发作有时者，是血结而不行，须小柴胡汤散之。二者既有留邪，必须治之可也。若发热经水适来，昼日明了，暮则讝语，此则经水既来，以里无留邪，但不妄犯，热随血散必自愈。经曰：血自下，下者愈。故无犯胃气及上二焦，必自愈。所谓妄犯者，谓恐以讝语为阳明内实，攻之犯其胃气也；此无胸胁之邪，恐刺期门，犯其中焦也；此无血结，恐与小柴胡汤，犯其上焦也。小柴胡汤解散则动卫气，卫出上焦，动卫气是犯上焦也。刺期门则动荣气，荣出中焦，动荣气是犯中焦也。《脉经》有曰：无犯肾气及上二焦，岂谓药不谓针耶？
　　　　儒门事亲 【元　张从政】

　　　　　月事沉滞

　　夫妇人月事沉滞，数月不行，肌肉不减，《内经》曰：此名为瘕为沉也。沉者，月事沉滞不行也，急宜服桃仁承气汤加当归，大作剂料服，不过三服立愈。后用四物汤补之，更可用《宣明方》槟榔丸。[29p]

When periodic chills and fevers occur at times like malaria, it is due to blood congestion and stagnation. One should disperse it with Xiao Chai Hu Decoction. If there are lingering pathogens present, they must be treated. If a fever arises with menstruation arriving on schedule, clearly during the day and accompanied by vague speech at night, this indicates that with the arrival of menstruation, there are no lingering pathogens left; as long as one does not interfere recklessly, the heat will disperse with the blood and will naturally recover. The text states: "Blood descends; when it descends, recovery occurs." Therefore, one should not disturb the stomach qi or the upper jiao, and recovery will happen on its own. Reckless interference refers to the fear that vague speech may be interpreted as an excess in the Yangming channel, thus attacking it and disturbing stomach qi; if there is no pathogen in the chest and flanks, one fears to needling the Qi men point, disturbing the middle jiao; if there is no blood congestion, one fears that Xiao Chai Hu Decoction will interfere with the upper jiao. When Xiao Chai Hu Decoction disperses, it moves the defensive qi, which originates from the upper jiao; thus, moving the defensive qi disturbs the upper jiao. Needling the Qi men also stimulates the nutritive qi, which arises from the middle jiao; thus, moving the nutritive qi disturbs the middle jiao. The "Pulse Canon" states: One should not disturb the kidney qi or the upper two jiao; does this mean it refers to medicine but not needles?

Regarding women’s menstruation stagnation:

If a woman’s menstruation is stagnant and fails to come for several months, without muscle loss, the "Inner Canon" states that this is called a mass or stagnation. Stagnation refers to menstruation that is blocked and not flowing; it is urgent to take Tao Ren Cheng Qi Decoction plus Angelica, in a sufficient dosage, and after just three doses, recovery will be immediate. Afterwards, one can use Si Wu Decoction to replenish; additionally, one may use the "Xuanming Fang" Betel Nut Pill.[29p]

　　　　　经血暴下

　　夫妇人年及五十以上，经血暴下者，妇人经血，终于七七之数，数外暴下，《内经》曰：火主暴速，亦因暴喜暴怒忧结惊恐之致然也，慎不可作冷病治之。如下峻热之药则死。止可用黄连解毒汤以清于上，更用莲壳灰、棕毛以渗于下，然后用四物汤加延胡索散，凉血和经之药是也。
　　　　　月事不来

　　夫妇人有月事不来者，室女亦然。《内经》曰：月事不来者，是胞脉闭也。胞脉者属火而络于脬中，令气上迫肺，心气不得下通，故月事不来也。可用茶调散吐之；吐讫，可用玉烛散、当归散或三和汤、桂苓白朮散、柴胡饮子，量虚实选而用之。降心火，益肾水，开胃进食，分阴阳，利水道之药是也。慎勿服峻热之药。若服之，则变成肺痿骨蒸潮热，咳嗽咯脓，呕血而喘，小便濇滞，寝汗不已，渐至形瘦脉大。虽遇良医，亦成不救。[30p]

Sudden Menstrual Flow

For women aged fifty and above, if there is a sudden menstrual flow, it is said that the menstrual blood reaches its full count at seventy-seven. Beyond that, a sudden flow occurs. The Inner Canon states that fire governs sudden occurrences, which may also be due to extreme joy, anger, worry, distress, or fright. Therefore, one must be cautious not to treat this as a cold illness. If treated with severe heat medicines, it may be fatal. One may only use Huanglian Jiedu Decoction to clear the upper parts, and then use lotus shell ash and palm hair to filter downward. Following that, use Siwu Decoction with Yanhusuo powder; these serve to cool the blood and regulate the menstrual flow.

Delayed Menstruation

For women who have delayed menstruation, the same is true for unmarried girls. The Inner Canon states that when menstruation does not come, it is due to the closure of the胞脉 (bao mai). The胞脉 is associated with fire and is linked to the kidneys, causing qi to rise and press on the lungs, preventing heart qi from descending, hence the absence of menstruation. One may use tea to adjust a purging powder; after purging, one can utilize Yuzhu powder, Danggui powder, or Sanhe Decoction, Guiling Baizhu powder, and Chaihu Decoction, choosing according to the condition of excess and deficiency. The aim is to descend heart fire, nourish kidney water, stimulate appetite, balance yin and yang, and facilitate urination. Care must be taken to avoid harsh, heating medications. If taken, it may result in lung atrophy, bone steaming, tidal fever, cough with purulent sputum, vomiting blood and wheezing, difficulty in urination, persistent sweating during sleep, progressively leading to emaciation and a large pulse. Even with a good physician, it would be beyond cure.[30p]

　　　　东垣十书 【元　李杲】

　　　　　经闭有三

　　阴阳别论云：二阳之病发心脾，有不得隐曲，女子不月，其传为风消，为息贲者，死不治。妇人脾胃久虚，或形羸气血俱衰，而致经水断绝不行；或病中消胃热，善食渐瘦，津液不生。夫经者，血脉津液所化，津液既绝，为热所烁，肌肉消瘦，时见燥渴，血海枯竭，病名曰血枯经绝，宜泻胃之燥热，补益气血，经自行矣。此证或经适行而有子，子不安为胎病者有矣，或心包脉洪数，躁作时见，大便秘濇，小便虽清不利，而经水闭绝不行，此乃血海干枯，宜调血脉，除包络中火邪而经自行矣。《内经》所谓小肠移热于大肠，为症瘕，为沉。脉濇不利，则月事沉滞而不利，故云为症瘕为沉也。或因劳心、心火上行，月事不来，安心和血泻火，经自行矣。故《内经》云：月事不来者，胞脉闭也。胞脉者属心而络于胞中，今气上迫肺，心气不得下，故月事不来也。[31p]

On the Three Causes of Menstrual Cessation

The "Treatise on Yin and Yang" states: When diseases of the two Yang elements affect the heart and spleen, there may be hidden paths that become obstructed. If a woman does not have her monthly flow, this is referred to as "wind consumed" or "breath of vitality ceases," and if untreated, it can lead to death. Women with prolonged deficiency of the spleen and stomach, or who are emaciated with weakened vital energy and blood, may experience a complete cessation of menstruation. This could also be due to heat digestion during illness, leading to gradual weakness and the absence of bodily fluids. The menstrual flow is produced from the transformation of blood and fluids; if these fluids are exhausted, and heat consumes them, the muscles will wither, thirst may arise, and the blood reservoir will be depleted. This condition is termed "blood withered, menstruation ceased," and it is advisable to drain the stomach of its dry heat and to tonify vital energy and blood; the menstruation will then resume.

In some cases, the menstrual flow may be obstructed by pregnancy, and if the fetus is unsteady due to fetal disease, this can occur. If the pericardium pulse is abundant and rapid, accompanied by agitation, with constipation observed, and even though the urination seems clear, menstruation remains blocked and ceases. This indicates that the blood reservoir is dried up, and it is necessary to regulate the blood vessels and expel the internal fire evil from the pericardium to restore the menstrual flow.

The "Internal Classic" mentions that heat from the small intestine may move to the large intestine, resulting in stagnation or accumulation. When the pulse is shallow and obstructed, menstruation becomes stagnant and fails to flow, which is why it is described as stagnation or accumulation. Alternatively, overwork and heart fire rising may cause a delay in menstruation; calming the heart and harmonizing the blood, draining the fire will then allow for menstruation to resume. Thus, the "Internal Classic" states that when menstruation does not arrive, it is the blockage of the uterine vessels. These vessels are associated with the heart and connect within the uterus; currently, the energy pressing upward onto the lungs inhibits the heart’s energy from descending, which is why menstruation does not occur.[31p]

　　　　　闭属少阳
　　凡妇人女子之病，经水适断，俱作少阳治之，伤寒杂病一体。经云：身有病而有邪，经脉闭也。又云：月事不来者，胞脉闭也。经闭者尺中不至，胞闭者生化绝源，二者皆血病也，厥阴主之。厥阴病则少阳病矣，累及其夫也。治之之法，或实作大热，或变成劳，脉有浮中沉之不同，故有药表里和之不一，察其在气在血，定其行阴行阳。使大小不失其宜，轻重各得其所，逆从缓急，举无不当，则可以万全矣。此少阳一治，不可不知也。　　凡治杂病，先调其气，次疗诸疾，无损胃气，是其要也。若血受病，亦先调气，谓气不调则血不行。又气为之纲，夫也。夫不唱，妇不随也。故妇人病经，先柴胡以行经之表，次四物以行经之里，先气而后血也。[32p]

Treatment of Lesser Yang

For women’s ailments, when menstrual flow is disrupted, all are treated as Lesser Yang conditions, encompassing both cold and miscellaneous diseases. The classic texts state: when the body is ill and there is an external pathogen, the meridians are obstructed. Moreover, if the monthly cycle does not come, it signifies obstruction in the conception vessels. In cases where menstruation is obstructed, the pulse at the wrist fails to show, and when the conception vessel is obstructed, the source of life is cut off; both scenarios involve blood disorders, which are under the domain of the Jueyin. If one suffers from a Jueyin condition, it then becomes a Lesser Yang condition, and this can affect the husband as well.

The methods of treatment may involve creating intense heat or transforming into exhaustion; the pulse may exhibit both superficial and deep characteristics, requiring differing herbs for interior and exterior harmonization. One must assess whether the issues reside in qi or blood, and determine if they address Yin or Yang. It is essential that the dosages for both large and small are appropriately balanced, with light and heavy matters serving their place, considering reversals and urgency, managing everything without error, thus achieving total wellness. This method of treating Lesser Yang is vital knowledge.

In treating miscellaneous diseases, one must first harmonize the qi, followed by addressing various ailments, ensuring that the stomach qi remains unharmed—which is critical. If blood is affected, qi must still be adjusted first, as unharmonized qi means blood cannot circulate. Qi serves as the fundamental substance; it is like the husband. If the husband does not sing, the wife will not follow. Therefore, for women’s menstrual disorders, one begins with Chaihu to regulate the exterior of the menstrual cycle and then follows with the Four Substances to nourish the interior, prioritizing qi before blood.[32p]

　　　　　不调治法

　　妇人经水不调，右尺脉按之空虚，是气血俱脱，大寒证。轻手其脉数疾，举指弦紧或濇，皆阳脱之证，阴火亦亡。见热证于口鼻眼或渴，此皆阴躁阳欲去也，当温之降之，引之燥之，用升阳举经汤。此法大升浮血气，补命门之下脱也。[33p]

Method for Imbalance in Women

When a woman has an irregular menstrual flow, and the right pulse at the wrist feels empty, this indicates a loss of both qi and blood, resulting in a cold condition. If the pulse is rapid and quick with a tense or weak feeling, it suggests a deficiency of yang, and the yin fire is also diminished. If there are signs of heat in the mouth, nose, eyes, or thirst, this indicates yin agitation and the desire for yang to depart. In this case, one should warm and reduce, drawing out the dryness, using the Shengyang Jujing Decoction. This method greatly elevates and replenishes the floating blood and qi, replenishing the deficiency in the life gate below.[33p]

　　　　　热入血室治法

　　昼则明了，夜则讝语，热入血室，无犯胃气及上二焦，不治自愈。若甚则四顺饮子、桃仁承气汤，证相似当下者用之。
　　　　丹溪心法 【元　朱震亨】

　　　　　经水证治

　　妇人经水过期，血水也，四物加参、朮；带痰加南星、半夏、陈皮之类。经水不及期而来者，血热也，四物加黄连。过期紫黑有块，亦血热也，必作痛，四物加香附、黄连。过期色淡者，痰多也，二陈加川芎、当归。过期而来，乃是血虚，宜补血，用四物加黄芪、陈皮、升麻。未及期先来，乃是气血俱热，宜凉气血，柴胡、黄芩、当归、白芍、生地，香附之属。　　经不调而血色淡，宜补气血，参、芪、芎、归，香附、白勺；腹痛加胶珠、艾叶、延胡索。[34p]

Treatment for Heat Entering the Blood Chamber

During the day, clarity prevails; at night, there are incoherent words. Heat enters the blood chamber, but does not violate the stomach qi and the two upper jiaos; it can heal on its own. If severe, use the Four Gentlemen Decoction, or Peach Kernel Decoction for situations that resemble the condition described.
— Danxi's Heart Method (Yuan, Zhu Zhenheng)

Treatment for Menstrual Disorders

For women whose menstruation is overdue, the blood may be stagnant; use Four Substances with Ginseng and Atractylodes. If there is phlegm, add South Star, Pinellia, and Dried Citrus Peel. If menstruation arrives before the expected time, it is due to blood heat; use Four Substances with Coptis. If overdue and the blood is dark purple with clots, it is also due to blood heat and will likely cause pain; use Four Substances with Cyperus and Coptis. If overdue and the color is pale, there is excess phlegm; use Two Aged Herbs with Chuanxiong and Angelica. If it arrives overdue, it indicates blood deficiency; it is advisable to tonify the blood with Four Substances, adding Astragalus, Dried Citrus Peel, and Cimicifuga. If it arrives early, both qi and blood are hot; it is advised to cool the qi and blood using Chaihu, Huangqin, Angelica, White Peony, Rehmannia, and similar herbs. If menstruation is irregular and the blood color is pale, tonify qi and blood using Ginseng, Astragalus, Chuanxiong, Angelica, plus Cyperus and White Peony; for abdominal pain, add Gelatin Pearl, Mugwort, and Corydalis.[34p]

　　经候过而作痛者，乃虚中有热，所以作疼。经水将来作疼者，血实也【一云气滞，】 四物加桃仁、黄连、香附。临行时腰疼腹痛，乃是郁滞有瘀血，宜四物加红花、桃仁、莪朮、延胡索、香附、木香；发热加黄芩、柴胡。紫色成块者，热也，四物加黄连、柴胡之类。　　痰多占住血海地位，因而下多者，目必渐昏。肥人如此，用南星、苍朮、川芎、香附，作丸子服之。肥人不及日数而多者，痰多血虚有热，亦用前丸药中，更加黄连、白朮丸服。　　血枯经闭者，四物加桃仁、红花。[35p]

When pain occurs after the menstrual period, it is due to heat within the deficiency, which causes the pain. If pain occurs just before the menstrual flow, it indicates that the blood is abundant. [Some say it is due to Qi stagnation.] For treatment, use the four substance formula with the addition of peach kernel and coptis. If there is lower back and abdominal pain before the onset of menstruation, it is due to stagnation and the presence of stagnant blood; in this case, it is advisable to use the four substance formula with safflower, peach kernel, curcuma, yan hu suo, cyperus, and wood fragrance. If there is fever, add scutellaria and bupleurum. If there are purple spots, it indicates heat; in this case, add coptis and bupleurum to the four substance formula.

If there is an excessive amount of phlegm occupying the blood sea position, then one will gradually experience vision deterioration. For obese individuals with this condition, use nux vomica, aster, ligusticum wallichii, and cyperus, making them into pills to be taken. If an obese person has an excessive amount before their due time, it indicates excessive phlegm and blood deficiency with heat; use the previous pill formula and additionally include coptis and white atractylodes.

For those with blood depletion resulting in amenorrhea, use the four substance formula with the addition of peach kernel and safflower.[35p]

躯脂满经闭者，以导痰汤加黄连、川芎。不可服地黄，泥膈故也，如用以姜汁炒。　　肥胖饮食过度之人，而经水不调者，乃是湿痰，宜苍朮、半夏、滑石、茯苓、白朮、香附、川芎、当归。　　临经来时肚痛者，四物汤加陈皮、延胡索、牡丹皮、甘草。痛甚者豆淋酒，痛缓者童便煮莎根，入炒条芩末为丸。　　经水去多不能住者，以三补丸加莎根、龟板、金毛狗脊。　　阴虚经脉久不通，小便濇，身体疼痛，以四物加苍朮、牛膝、陈皮，生甘草；又用苍莎丸加苍耳。[36p]

For a person with an excess of body fat and a closed menstrual cycle, use a phlegm-dissolving decoction with added Huanglian and Chuanxiong. Avoid using Dihuang, as it can lead to stagnation. If prepared with ginger juice, it becomes more adverse.

For those who are overweight and have irregular menstrual flow due to excessive damp phlegm, the recommended ingredients are Cangzhu, Banxia, Huashi, Fuling, Baizhu, Xiangfu, Chuanxiong, and Danggui.

For those who experience abdominal pain when menstruation approaches, use the Siwu Decoction with added Chenpi, Yanhusuo, Mudanpi, and Licorice. For severe pain, use Doulin wine; for milder pain, boil Shagen (a type of grass root) in children's urine and incorporate fried Qiaoqing powder into pills.

If menstruation is excessive and difficult to control, use Sanbu Pills with Shagen, Gui Ban, and Jinmao Goujizi.

For those with a long-lasting deficiency in the Yin and blocked meridians, experiencing frequent urination and bodily pain, incorporate Siwu Decoction with Cangzhu, Niuxi, Chenpi, and raw Licorice; additionally, use Cangsha Pills combined with Canger.[36p]

酒芍药为丸，就煎前药吞下。经候微少，渐渐不通，手足烦疼，渐瘦生潮热，脉微数，四物汤去地黄，川芎，如泽兰叶三倍，甘草半分。　　经水过多，四物汤去熟地黄加生地，或只加黄芩、白朮。　　经行身热，脉数头昏，四物汤加柴胡、黄芩。　　经行微少，或胀或疼，四肢疼痛，四物汤加延胡、没药、白芷为末，淡酢汤调下。　　经候不调，心腹(疒丂)痛，只用芎、归二味，名君臣散。　　经欲行，脐腹绞痛，四物加延胡、槟榔、苦楝炒、木香减半。　　经水濇少，四物加葵花、红花。[37p]

When using wine and peony root to make pills, swallow them before brewing the medicine. If the menstruation is slightly delayed, and gradually becomes obstructed, with discomfort in the hands and feet, increasing thinness and hot flashes, and a weak, rapid pulse, modify the Four Substance Decoction by removing cooked Rehmannia and adding three times the amount of ligusticum, along with half a part of licorice.

If the menstrual flow is excessive, modify the Four Substance Decoction by removing cooked Rehmannia and adding raw Rehmannia, or simply add Scutellaria and Atractylodes.

If there are body heat and a rapid pulse during the menstrual period, along with dizziness, add Chaihu and Scutellaria to the Four Substance Decoction.

If the menstrual flow is slightly reduced, accompanied by distention or pain, and pain in the limbs, add Yanhusuo, myrrh, and angelica dahurica as a powder to the Four Substance Decoction, mixing it with a light vinegar decoction.

If the menstrual cycle is irregular and there is pain in the heart and abdomen, use only the two herbs, ligusticum and angelica, known as the monarch-minister powder.

If menstrual onset is accompanied by cramping pain in the lower abdomen, add Yanhusuo, areca nut, and half the amount of fried neem, along with wood incense.

If the menstrual flow is scant, add sunflower and safflower to the Four Substance Decoction.[37p]

　　经候过而作痛。气血俱虚也，宜四物对四君子汤服之。　　经水色淡者，气血俱虚也，宜八物汤之类。八物者，四物、四君子也。如兼他证，随证加药。　　月候不调之由，或前或后，或多或少。凡行后作痛者虚也，少而淡者血虚也，多者气虚也，其将行作痛及凝块不散者滞也，紫黑色者滞而挟热也。　　经水或前或后，或多或少，或逾月一至，或一月再至，皆不调之故，治之宜调经散。　　经候不调，当以四物汤为主治。
　　月候不调之中，有兼疼痛者，有兼发热者，有趱前者，有退后者，则趱前为热，退后为虚也。疼痛之中，有常时作痛者，有经前经后作痛者，则常时与经前作痛者为血积，经后为血虚也。发热之中，有常时发热者，有经行发热者，则常时为血虚有积，经行为血虚有热也。　　经水濇少，为虚为濇，虚则补之，濇则需之。[38p]

When menstruation is delayed and pain occurs, it indicates deficiency of both qi and blood, and one should take the Four Substances Decoction paired with the Four Gentlemen Decoction. If the menstrual blood is pale, it also indicates deficiency of qi and blood, and one should use something like the Eight Substances Decoction. The Eight Substances include the Four Substances and the Four Gentlemen. If there are accompanying symptoms, additional herbs should be added according to those symptoms.

The causes of menstrual irregularities can be either occurring earlier or later, or having more or less blood flow. Generally, pain occurring after menstruation indicates deficiency; if the flow is light and pale, it denotes blood deficiency; if it’s heavy, it reflects qi deficiency. Pain that will occur and does not resolve indicates stagnation, while dark purple or black blood indicates stagnation with accompanying heat.

Menstrual blood may come earlier or later, in greater or lesser amounts, or may come once a month or twice in a month; these are all signs of irregularities. Treatment should aim to regulate and disperse the menstruation.

For irregular menstrual cycles, the main treatment should be the Four Substances Decoction. Among those with menstrual irregularities, some may also experience pain, fever, early menstruation, or delayed menstruation. Early menstruation indicates heat, while delayed menstruation indicates deficiency. Pain can occur consistently or just before and after menstruation; consistent pain and pain before menstruation indicate blood accumulation, while pain after menstruation indicates blood deficiency.

Among those who experience fever, some may have constant fevers, while others may have fevers during menstruation; constant fevers indicate blood deficiency with accumulation, while fevers during menstruation indicate blood deficiency with heat.

If menstrual flow is scant, it indicates either deficiency or a thin flow; deficiency requires supplementation, while thin flow requires assistance.[38p]

　　　　格致余论 【元　朱震亨】

　　　　　辨紫黑痛块

　　经水者，阴血也。阴必从阳，故其色红，禀火色也。血为气之配，气热则热，气寒则寒，气升则升，气降则降，气凝则凝，气滞则滞，气清则清，气浊则浊。往往见有成块者，气之凝也。将行而痛者，气之滞也。来后作痛者，气血俱虚也。色淡者，亦虚也。错经妄行者，气之乱也。紫者，气之热也。黑者，热之甚也。人但见其紫者、黑者、作痛者、成块者，率指为风冷而行温热之剂，祸不旋踵矣。良由《病源》论月水诸病皆曰风冷乘之，宜其相习而成俗也。或曰：黑，北方水之色也，紫淡于黑，非冷而何？余日：经曰，亢则害，承乃制。热甚者必兼水化，所以热则紫，甚则黑也。况妇人性执而见鄙，嗜欲加倍，脏腑厥阳之火，无日不起。非热而何？若夫风冷必须外得，设或有之，盖千百而一二者也。[39p]

On the Distinction of Purple and Black Painful Masses

The menstrual flow is associated with Yin blood. Yin must derive from Yang, hence it is red, which embodies the color of fire. Blood is paired with Qi; when Qi is hot, it becomes hot, and when Qi is cold, it becomes cold. When Qi rises, it rises; when it descends, it descends; when Qi condenses, it condenses; when Qi stagnates, it stagnates; when Qi is clear, it is clear; when Qi is turbid, it is turbid. Often, masses are seen to form due to the condensation of Qi. Pain that occurs upon movement is due to the stagnation of Qi. Pain that arises afterward indicates deficiency in both Qi and blood. A pale color also signifies deficiency. Erratic movement of the menstrual flow indicates chaotic Qi. Purple indicates hot Qi, while black indicates extreme heat. People often see the purple, black, painful masses and hastily attribute them to wind and cold, treating them with warming remedies, leading to disaster. This is likely due to the theory in "Sources of Disease," which states that all monthly conditions are said to be caused by wind and cold, making it a common practice.

Some say: Black is the color of northern water, and purple is lighter than black; how can it not be cold? I respond: The classics state that excess causes harm, and holding onto it must be controlled. When heat is excessive, it must also be accompanied by the transformation of water, thus the heat appears purple and extreme heat appears black. Moreover, women are inherently more reclusive and possess heightened desires; the yang fire of their organs is constantly active. How can this not be heat? As for wind and cold, they must be obtained from the outside; if they are present, it is but one in a thousand or one in two.[39p]

　　　　溯洄集 【元　王履】

　　　　　二阳病论

　　经曰：二阳之病发心脾，有不得隐曲，女子不月。释之者，谓男子则脾受之而味不化，故少精；女子则心受之，而血不流，故不月。分心脾为男女各受立说。窃独谓不然。夫二阳，阳明也，胃与大肠之脉也。肠胃有病，心脾受之。发心脾，犹言延及于心脾也。-虽然，脾胃为合，胃病而及脾，理固宜矣。大肠与心，本非合也，今大肠而及心，何哉？盖胃为受纳之腑，大肠为传化之腑。[40p]

On the Illness of the Two Yangs

The text says: "The illness of the two Yangs affects the heart and spleen, causing inability to conceal and resulting in women not menstruating." Those who explain this state that for men, the spleen is affected, leading to insufficient essence; for women, the heart is affected, causing a lack of menstrual flow. They divide the heart and spleen to argue that each gender has a distinct cause.

I privately disagree with this interpretation. The term "two Yangs" refers to Yangming, which pertains to the stomach and large intestine channels. When there is illness in the intestines and stomach, it affects the heart and spleen. "Affecting the heart and spleen" means that the influence extends to these organs. Indeed, the spleen and stomach are interrelated, so when there is a stomach ailment, it naturally impacts the spleen. However, the large intestine and heart are not usually interconnected; thus, why does a large intestine issue impact the heart? This is because the stomach is the organ of reception, while the large intestine is the organ of transformation and transmission.[40p]

食入于胃，浊气归心，饮入于胃，输精于脾者，以胃之能纳，肠之能化耳。肠胃既病，则不能受，不能化，心脾何所资乎？心脾既无所资，则无所运化而生精血矣。故肠胃有病，心脾受之，则男为少精，女为不月矣。心脾当总言，男女不当分说，至隐曲不月，方可分说耳。若如释者之言，则男之精独资于脾而不资于心。女之血独资于心而不资于脾，有是理耶！盖男女之精血，皆由五脏六腑之相养而后成，可谓之男精资于脾，女血资于心乎？经本曰：男女皆有心脾之病，但在男子则隐曲之不利，在女子则月事之不来耳。[41p]

Food enters the stomach, and the turbid qi returns to the heart; drink enters the stomach and is processed by the spleen. This is due to the stomach’s ability to receive and the intestines’ ability to transform. When the intestines and stomach are ill, they cannot receive or transform, and what then can the heart and spleen depend on? Once the heart and spleen have no resources to depend on, they cannot function to produce vital essence and blood. Thus, when the intestines and stomach are sick, the heart and spleen are affected, leading to men having low sperm production and women having irregular menstrual cycles.

The heart and spleen should be considered together; one should not divide the discussion by gender. Only in cases of hidden menstrual irregularities can one speak separately about men and women. If we follow the claims made by some monks, it suggests that male essence relies solely on the spleen and not on the heart, while female blood relies solely on the heart and not on the spleen. Is there any validity in this? In truth, both male essence and female blood are nourished through the balance of the five viscera and six bowels before they are formed, so can we really say that male essence relies on the spleen and female blood relies on the heart? The classics state that both men and women may suffer from heart and spleen diseases, but in men, this manifests as hidden issues affecting fertility, while in women, this presents as the absence of menstrual flow.[41p]

　　　　卫生宝鉴 【元　罗天益】

　　　　　热入血室成结胸

　　或问：热入血室，何为而成结胸也？余曰：邪气传入经络作主，气相搏，上下流行，遇经水适来适断，邪气乘虚入于血室，血为邪所迫，入于肝经，肝受邪则讝语而见鬼，复入膻中则血结于胸中。何以言之？妇人平居，水养木，血养肝，方未受孕则以之为月水，既妊则中蓄之以养胎，及已产则上壅之以为乳汁，皆血之所为也。今邪逐血，并归于肝经，聚于膻中，结于乳下，故手触之则痛，非药可及，故当刺期门也。[42p]

Hygienic Treasure (Yuan Dynasty, Luo Tianyi)

Heat Enters the Blood Chamber, Resulting in Chest Accumulation

Someone asked: What causes heat to enter the blood chamber and result in chest accumulation? I replied: The pathogenic qi enters the meridians as the master, causing the energies to clash and flow up and down. When it meets the menstrual flow, it disrupts it; the pathogenic qi then takes advantage of the weakness to enter the blood chamber. The blood, being forced by the pathogenic influence, enters the liver meridian. When the liver is affected by the pathogen, it leads to speech difficulties and hallucinatory experiences. This further enters the diaphragm, causing blood to accumulate in the chest. How do I explain this? A woman, in her normal state, has water nourishing wood and blood nourishing the liver. Before conception, this blood serves as menstruation; once pregnant, it is reserved to nurture the fetus. After giving birth, it is transformed to produce milk. All of these functions depend on blood. Now, when the pathogen drives out the blood and it returns to the liver meridian, it accumulates in the diaphragm and solidifies beneath the breast, hence causing pain upon touch. This condition cannot be treated with medicine; therefore, the point to be needled is Qimen.[42p]

　　　　证治要诀 【明　戴思恭】

　　　　　经事不调

　　妇人每月经水应期而下，不使有余，犹太阴之缺也。其有或先或后，或少或多，或欲来先病，或遇来而断续，皆谓之不调，和气饮加香附子半钱，兼咽独附丸。经事来而腹痛者，经事不来而腹亦痛者，皆血之不调故也。欲调其血，先调其气，四物汤加吴茱萸半钱、香附子一钱，和气饮加茱萸半钱方可用。痛甚者，延胡索汤。然又恐感外邪、饮食致痛，痛不因血，尤宜详审，和气饮却能兼治。[43p]

Essentials of Diagnosis and Treatment

Ming - Dai Sigong

Menstrual Irregularities

A woman’s menstrual flow should arrive punctually each month, not exceeding or lacking, similar to the deficiency of the Yin. If it comes either early or late, or is too scanty or excessive, or if there is pain before or during menstruation, these are all referred to as irregularities. The remedy for this includes herbal formulas to harmonize Qi, such as Heqi Decoction with half a qian of Xiangfuzi, and adding Yandu Pill. If menstruation arrives with abdominal pain, or if there is abdominal pain without menstruation, both are due to the disharmony of blood. To remedy blood imbalance, one must first regulate Qi. The Siwu Decoction with half a qian of Wuzhuyu and one qian of Xiangfuzi may be used, along with Heqi Decoction with half a qian of Zhuyujie. For severe pain, Yan Hu Suo Decoction is recommended. However, care must be taken to guard against external pathogens or dietary causes of pain, especially if the pain is not due to blood. Thus, it is necessary to conduct a detailed examination, and Heqi Decoction can also treat the accompanying conditions.[43p]

　　有因惊气上逆，致月不通，涎多神昏，皆则不知人；或妄言歌笑，似心疯，似五癎，醒时又似正人；或病来身如摇动，手足如搐搦，四七汤、大温经汤各半贴，和匀服。　　有经候失期，或过二三月变生诸证者。和气饮须用桂枝者，性最动血。和气饮加苏木、红花、干漆各半钱，桃仁一钱，或酢或酒煎去滓，入麝香少许，仍以酢调黑神散。　　因血瘀而腹内有块者，四物汤去地黄加官桂、白朮各半钱。　　因经候不调，血不循故道，从粪后出，腹或疼或不疼，勿作寻常便血治，宜顺其经，四物汤去地黄加阿胶、香附子各一钱，仍以黑神散和调气散，白汤点服。[44p]

Due to fear and anxiety causing qi to rise, resulting in the moon not flowing smoothly, excessive phlegm, and a muddled spirit, one may become unaware of their own person; or they might speak erratically, laugh, appearing mad, like one afflicted with five kinds of tremors, yet seem perfectly sane when awake; or when ill, the body feels as if it is shaking, with hands and feet twitching. Administer a mixture of "Four Seven Decoction" and "Great Warmth Classic Decoction" in equal parts, properly combined and consumed.

For those who miss their menstrual period or have symptoms appearing after two or three months, one should use Gui Zhi Decoction as it stirs the blood. Modify this decoction by adding half a coin each of Su Mu, Hong Hua, and Gan Qi—add a penny of Tao Ren, and either vinegar or wine to boil away the dregs, with a little musk added, and then mix it with vinegar to prepare Heishen Powder.

If there are lumps in the abdomen due to blood stasis, modify the Si Wu Decoction by removing Di Huang and adding half a coin each of Guan Gui and Bai Zhu.

For menstrual irregularities with blood not following its proper path, manifesting after bowel movements, causing abdominal pain or not, do not treat it like ordinary blood in stool; instead, one should follow the menstrual cycle. Use Si Wu Decoction, removing Di Huang and adding one penny each of Ejiao and Xiang Fu, then mix with Heishen Powder to adjust qi, taking it with clear soup as a remedy.[44p]

　　　　医学纲目 【明　楼英】

　　　　　调经

　　胎前之道，始于求子。求子之法，莫先调经。每见妇人之无子者。其经必或前或后，或多或少，或将行作痛，或行后作痛，或紫或黑或淡，或凝而不调，不调则血气乖争，不能成孕矣。详夫不调之由，其或前或后，及行后作痛者，虚也；其少而淡者，血虚也；多者，气虚也；其将行作痛，及凝块不散者，滞也；紫黑色者，滞而挟热也。治法：血虚者四物，气虚者四物加参、芪，滞者香附、缩砂、木香、槟榔、桃仁、延胡，滞久而沉痼者，吐之下之，脉证热者四物加芩、连，脉证寒者四物加桂、附及紫石英之类是也。直至积去滞行虚回，然后血气和平，能孕子也。余每治经不调者，只一味香附末，酢为丸，服之亦百发百中也。[45p]

Medical Treatise: Adjusting the Menstrual Cycle

The way before conception begins is to seek a child. The method for seeking a child must start with regulating the menstrual cycle. Whenever I observe women who are childless, their menstruation is often irregular—either early or late, too much or too little, accompanied by pain before or after menstruation, and the color could be purple, black, or pale, or the flow is thick and unregulated. If the cycle is unregulated, then the blood and vital energy conflict and cannot achieve conception.

Let us explore the causes of this lack of regulation: if the cycle is early or late, accompanied by pain after menstruation, it indicates deficiency; if the flow is scanty and pale, it signifies blood deficiency; if it is excessive, it points to Qi deficiency; if there is pain before the cycle and clots that do not disperse, it signifies stagnation. If the color is purple or black, it indicates stagnation combined with heat.

The treatment methods are as follows: for blood deficiency, one should use the Four Substances Decoction; for Qi deficiency, the same plus ginseng and astragalus; for stagnation, one may use Xiangfu, Sande, Muxiang, Bitao, Taoren, and Yanhuhua. For prolonged stagnation that has become entrenched, methods such as vomiting or purging may be necessary. For those with a pulse and symptoms of heat, add Huangqin and Lian; for those with a pulse and symptoms of cold, add Gui, Fu, and varieties of quartz. Only after removing stagnation and restoring deficiency can blood and Qi harmonize, allowing for conception.

Whenever I treat cases of irregular menstruation, just one ingredient, powdered Xiangfu, formed into pills and taken, achieves consistent success.[45p]

　　　　　经水或前或后

　　妇人病多是月经乍多乍少，或前或后，时发疼痛，医者一类呼为经病，不曾说是阴胜阳，是阳胜阴，所以服药少效。盖阴气乘阳，则胞寒气冷，血不运行，经所谓天寒地冻，水凝成冰，故令乍少而在月后。若阳气乘阴，则血流散溢，经所谓天暑地热，经水沸溢，故令乍多而在月前。当别其阴阳，调其血气、使不相乘，以平为期，宜紫石英丸。[46p]

The menstrual flow may occur either sooner or later.

Women often experience irregularities in their menstruation, with periods that vary from heavy to light, or that arrive early or late, accompanied by pains. Physicians typically refer to this as menstrual illness, without distinguishing whether yin is overpowering yang or vice versa, resulting in ineffective treatments. When yin energy overtakes yang, the womb becomes cold due to this yin influence, leading to stagnant blood flow, which aligns with the concept that during cold weather, water freezes, hence the irregularities such as having a scanty flow after the period. Conversely, when yang energy overpowers yin, blood flows excessively and erratically; this occurs under hot conditions, where the menstrual flow is overly abundant, thus arriving before the expected time. It is essential to discern between yin and yang, harmonize blood and energy, preventing them from overpowering each other, ensuring a regular cycle. The recommended remedy is the Purple Quartz Pills.[46p]

　　　　　天癸过期

　　妇人天癸已过期，经脉不匀，或三四月不行，或一月再至，腰腹疼痛，《素问》云七损八益，谓女子七数尽而经不依时者，血有余也，不可止之，但令得依时不腰痛为善，宜当归散。
　　　　　热入血室

　　妇人伤寒中风，治法与男子无异，若热入血室则不同也，宜以四物汤安养经血，佐以汗下之药治之。　　妇人伤寒中风，自汗头痛，项背强，发热恶寒，脉浮而缓，恐热入血室，故用桂枝汤倍加芍药。　　妇人伤寒，脉浮而紧，头痛身热，恶寒无汗，恐热入血室，宜麻黄加生地汤。　　妇人伤寒，经脉方来初断，寒热如疟，狂言见鬼，宜用干姜柴胡汤。　　妇人室女，伤寒发热，经水适来适断，昼日明了，夜则讝语如见鬼神，宜小柴胡加生地汤。[47p]

On the Expiry of the Heavenly Period

When a woman's heavenly period has expired, her meridians are irregular; she may not menstruate for three or four months, or may have a monthly recurrence. If there is pain in the waist and abdomen, the Huangdi Neijing states that a woman's vitality decreases with age, and if her periods do not come on time, it indicates an excess of blood. It should not be stopped, but instead, the focus should be on regularity and alleviating waist pain, preferably using Danggui Powder.

Heat Enters the Blood Chamber

For women suffering from cold-induced fever, the treatment is no different from that for men. However, if heat enters the blood chamber, it is different; one should use Siwu Decoction to nourish the blood, supplemented with medications to induce sweating and relieve the condition.

For women with cold-induced fever, presenting with spontaneous sweating, headache, stiff neck and back, fever and chills, and a pulse that is floating and slow, it is feared that heat has entered the blood chamber; thus, Gui Zhi Decoction should be used with an increased amount of Shao Yao.

For women with cold-induced fever characterized by a floating and tight pulse, headache, body heat, chills without sweating, it is also feared that heat may have entered the blood chamber; therefore, Ma Huang Decoction should be administered, adding Sheng Di.

When a woman has cold-induced fever, with menstrual flow just beginning to cease, exhibiting chills and fever similar to malaria, and is speaking wildly as if seeing ghosts, Gan Jiang and Chai Hu Decoction is advised.

For young unmarried women experiencing cold-induced fever, with menstruation arriving and ceasing at the appropriate times, and clear-headed during the day but speaking nonsense at night as if seeing spiritual beings, Xiao Chai Hu Decoction should be combined with Sheng Di Decoction.[47p]

　　妇人伤寒身热，脉长而弦，属阳明少阳，往来寒热，夜躁昼宁，如见鬼状，经水适断，热入血室，不实满者，小柴胡加牡丹皮主之；大实满者，桃仁承气主之。　　妇人伤寒，头痛脉浮，医反下之，邪气乘虚而传于里，经水闭而不行，心下结硬，口燥舌干，寒热往来，狂言如见鬼状，脉沉而数者，当下之，宜小柴胡加芒硝、大黄汤主之。　　妇人伤寒，表虚自汗，身凉，四肢拘急，脉沉而迟，太阳标病，少阴本病，经水适断，宜桂枝加附子、红花汤。　　妇人伤寒，太阳标病，汗解表除，邪热内攻，热入血室，经水过多，无满实者，甘草芍药汤。[48p]

When a woman suffers from cold damage with fever, her pulse is long and wiry, indicating the Yangming and Shaoyang stages. There will be alternating chills and fever, restlessness at night and peace during the day, as if seeing ghosts. If her menstrual flow is irregular, with heat entering the blood chamber but not resulting in fullness, she should be treated with Xiao Chai Hu Tang plus Mu Dan Pi; if there is fullness, she should be treated with Tao Ren Cheng Qi Tang.

In cases where a woman suffers from cold damage, experiences headache, and has a floating pulse, if the doctor prescribes purging, the evil qi will take advantage of the deficiency and penetrate inward. If the menstrual flow is obstructed, with hardness under the heart, dry mouth, and a dry tongue, along with alternating chills and fevers, and a pulse that is deep and rapid, she should be purged with Xiao Chai Hu Tang plus Mang Xiao and Da Huang Tang.

When a woman suffers from cold damage, experiencing exterior deficiency with spontaneous sweating, coolness of the body, stiff and tense limbs, and a deep and slow pulse, this is attributed to the Taiyang channel disease, rooted in the Shaoyin. If her menstrual flow is irregular, she should be treated with Gui Zhi Tang plus Fu Zi and Hong Hua Tang.

For a woman suffering from cold damage where the Taiyang channel is involved, if sweating relieves the exterior and the evil heat attacks internally, leading to heat entering the blood chamber, with excessive menstrual flow but no fullness, she should be treated with Gan Cao Shao Yao Tang.[48p]

　　　　明医杂着 【明　王纶】

　　　　　经脉不行

　　妇人女子经脉不行，有脾胃损伤而致者，不可便认作经闭血死，轻用通经破血之药，遇有此证，便须审其脾胃如何。若因饮食劳倦损伤脾胃，少食恶食，泄泻疼痛；或因误服汗下攻伐药，伤其中气，以致血少而不行者，只宜补养脾胃，用白朮为君，茯苓、芍药为臣，佐以黄芪、甘草、陈皮、麦芽、川芎、当归、柴胡等药，脾旺则能生血而经自行矣。又有饮食积滞，致损脾胃者，亦宜消积补脾。若脾胃无病，果有血块凝结，方宜行血通经。　　【注　心脾平和，则百骸五脏皆润泽而经候如常，苟或心脾受伤，则血无所养，亦无所统，而月经不调矣。是故调经者，当理心脾为主，其详已见《良方》月水不调方论下。大凡调经之法，肝脾血燥，四物为主；肝脾血弱，补中益气为主；肝脾郁火，归脾汤为主；肝经怒火，加味逍遥散为主。病因多端，不能悉举，治当临证制宜可也。】[49p]

On Irregular Menstruation:

If a woman's menstruation is irregular due to damage to the spleen and stomach, it should not be hastily interpreted as a case of menstrual cessation and blood stagnation. The use of drastic medicine to promote menstruation and break up blood clots should be avoided. In such cases, one must carefully assess the condition of the spleen and stomach. If the irregularity arises from diet and fatigue leading to damage to the spleen and stomach, characterized by poor appetite, bad food, diarrhea, and pain; or if it results from mistakenly taking purgative or depleting medications that affect the inner energy, leading to insufficient blood flow, then it is advisable to nourish the spleen and stomach. One can use bai zhu (Atractylodes) as the main ingredient, with fu ling (Poria), xiao yao (Peony), and assist with huang qi (Astragalus), gan cao (Licorice), chen pi ( dried tangerine peel), mai ya (Barley), chuan xiong (Szechuan Lovage), dang gui (Angelica), chai hu (Bupleurum), and other herbs. When the spleen is strong, it can generate blood and the menstruation will resume naturally.

In cases where food stagnation damages the spleen and stomach, one should also aim to resolve the stagnation and tonify the spleen. If there are no issues with the spleen and stomach but indeed blood clots are formed, only then should one consider promoting blood circulation and regulating menstruation.

Note: When both the heart and spleen are in harmony, all the organs and tissues are nourished, and menstrual conditions are normal. However, if the heart and spleen are harmed, blood will not be nourished nor regulated, leading to menstrual irregularities. Thus, when regulating menstruation, the focus should be on harmonizing the heart and spleen, as previously discussed in "Liang Fang" under the section on irregular menstruation. Generally, methods to regulate menstruation include: if liver and spleen blood is dry, focus on Si Wu Decoction; if liver and spleen blood is weak, focus on Bu Zhong Yi Qi Decoction; if there is liver qi stagnation with heat, focus on Gui Pi Decoction; and if there is liver anger and heat, focus on a modified Xiao Yao San. The causes of illness are varied and cannot be exhaustively listed; treatment should be adaptable to each individual case.[49p]

　　　　医学入门 【明　李梴】

　　　　　月事不通

　　妇人以血为主，天真气降，壬癸水合，肾气全盛，血脉流行，常以三旬一见，以象月盈则亏，故曰月经。经行与产后一般，若其时余血一点未净，或外被风寒，及湿冷暑热邪气，或内伤生冷，七情郁结。为痰为瘀，凝积于中，曰血滞。或经止后，用力太过，入房太甚，及服食燥热，以致火动，邪气盛而精血衰，曰血枯。《良方》云：经后被惊，则血气错乱妄行，逆于上则从口鼻而出，逆于身则水血相搏变为水肿。恚怒则气血逆于腰腿、心腹、背胁、手足、之间重痛，经行则发，过期则止。怒极伤肝，则有眩运、呕血、瘰疬、血风、疮疡等病。加之经血渗漏于其间，遂成窍穴生疮，淋沥不断；湿热相搏，遂为崩带；血结于内，爱为症瘕。凡此变证百出，不过血滞与枯而已。但血滞亦有虚热，血枯亦有虚热，故重则经闭不通。以滞枯分言，轻则经水不调，止言虚与热而已。[50p]

Introduction to Medicine
[Ming - Li Zhan]

Menstrual Irregularities

Women are governed by blood; when the true essence descends, the Yin and Yang merge, the kidney energy is fully prosperous, and the blood circulates. This typically occurs once every three weeks, symbolizing the waxing and waning of the moon, thus referred to as menstruation. The flow of menstruation and postpartum recovery are similar; if there is residual blood remaining after the period, or if exposed to wind, cold, damp, heat, or harmful energies, or if internally injured by cold, or if emotional disturbances cause stagnation, it may result in phlegm or blood stasis. This condition is termed blood stagnation.

After menstruation, excessive exertion, too much intimacy, or ingestion of heated, dry foods can provoke fire, strengthen the harmful energies, and deplete essence and blood, leading to what is called blood depletion. The text "Good Formulas" states: if startled after menstruation, the blood and energy can become chaotic and might reverse; if it moves upwards, it may exit through the mouth and nose, and if it moves downwards, it can lead to water accumulation. Anger causes the energy and blood to rebel, resulting in severe pain in the waist, legs, heart, abdomen, back, flanks, hands, and feet. When menstruation occurs, symptoms arise; if overdue, they stop. Extreme anger damages the liver, resulting in dizziness, vomiting of blood, scrofula, blood wind, sores, and ulcers. Moreover, if menstrual blood leaks, it can create sores in the orifices, causing non-stop dripping; when damp heat combines, it may cause excessive menstruation; when blood stagnates internally, it leads to symptomatic masses.

All these varied symptoms stem from mere blood stagnation and depletion. However, blood stagnation can also have conditions of false heat, and blood depletion can likewise indicate false heat. Thus, severe cases can lead to amenorrhea (absence of menstruation). In terms of stagnation and depletion, mild cases will show menstrual irregularities, while solely considering deficiency and heat respectively.[50p]

　　血滞经闭宜破者，原因饮食热毒，或暴怒凝瘀积痰，直须大黄、干漆之类，推陈致新，俾旧血消而新血生也。若气旺血枯，起于劳役忧思，却宜温和滋补；或兼有痰火湿热，尤宜清之凉之。每以肉桂为佐者，热则血行也，但不可纯服峻药以亏阴道。至于耗气益血之说，虽女科要法，但血为气配，气热则热，气寒则寒，气升则升，气降则降，气行则行，气滞则滞。如果郁火气盛于血者，方可单香附散、抑气散，加木香、槟榔、枳壳以开郁行气。[51p]

For blood stagnation and menstrual blockage that should be resolved, the causes are dietary heat and toxins, or excessive anger causing condensation of blood and phlegm. One must use substances like rhubarb and related herbs to promote transformation, allowing old blood to dissipate and new blood to be generated. If vigorous energy depletes the blood due to overwork and worry, it is better to nourish gently and harmoniously. If there is also phlegm, fire, or damp heat present, it is essential to clear and cool these conditions. Cinnamon is often used as an adjunct because it promotes blood circulation when there is heat, but one must not take harsh drugs that harm the Yin. Regarding the theory of depleting Qi while enhancing blood, although it is essential in gynecology, blood is paired with Qi. When Qi is hot, the blood is hot; when Qi is cold, the blood is cold; when Qi rises, it rises; when Qi descends, it descends; when Qi circulates, it circulates; when Qi stagnates, it stagnates. If there is accumulated fire energy in the blood, one may use Xiao Feng San or Qi regulating powder, supplemented with aromatics, areca nut, and bitter orange peel to open the stagnation and move the Qi.[51p]

若气乱则调，气冷则温，气虚则补，男女一般。盖阳生则阴自长，气衰则血亦涸，岂可专耗其气耶？论者多泥叔和血旺气衰，不知叔和论肝肺二脉，则宜肝旺于肺；其实气血平和，乃能有孕，故继曰两脏通和。但妇人见偏性鄙，婢妾志不得伸，郁怒无时不起，故香附为女人仙药。经曰：邪气盛则实，正气夺则虚。可不悟诸！　　经行登厕，风寒入内，以致凝濇，小温经汤。经行适来，续得寒热，就闭不通，或寒或暑，俱谓之热入血室，小柴胡汤加生地，或黄芩芍药汤加生地。[52p]

When the qi is disturbed, it must be regulated; when the qi is cold, it needs warmth; when the qi is weak, it should be replenished; this applies to both men and women. Indeed, when the yang is strong, the yin naturally grows; when the qi is depleted, the blood will also decrease. Can one solely exhaust their qi? Many scholars mistakenly follow Shuhe, who argues that strong blood leads to weak qi, not realizing that Shuhe discusses the liver and lung meridians, implying that the liver should be strong compared to the lungs; in truth, a balance of qi and blood is necessary for conception, hence the saying, "the two organs must be harmonized." Yet women often face bias, and their aspirations remain unfulfilled. They frequently experience pent-up emotions and anger; thus, Xiangfu is considered a miraculous herb for women. The classics state: when pathogenic qi is excessive, there is fullness; when the right qi is lacking, there is emptiness. Must one not understand this?

During menstruation, if one experiences wind and cold entering the body, it can lead to stagnation and clotted blood; a slight warming medicinal soup is recommended. If menstruation is accompanied by a sudden onset of cold and heat, resulting in a blockage, whether it is cold or heat, it is all referred to as heat entering the blood chamber; one can use Xiao Chai Hu Tang with Sheng Di Huang, or Huang Qin Shao Yao Tang with Sheng Di Huang.[52p]

经行过飧生冷，或外被冷湿，以致瘀血凝结者，五积散去麻黄加牡丹皮、红花。　　七情心气郁结不行者，分心气饮去羌活、半夏、桑皮、青皮，加川芎、当归、香附、莪朮、延胡索。有火者，更加黄芩，或小调经散、单香附丸。　　气血盛实，经络遏闭，或时挟痰者，单大黄膏；或马鞭草取汁熬膏为丸或烧存性，红花当归煎汤下。　　内伤饮食，劳倦损伤，脾胃气弱，体倦发热，腹痛肠鸣，饮食减少而不生血者，补中益气汤加川芎、生地、天花粉。肠鸣月水不来者，病在胃，胃虚不生血气，宜单厚朴五钱，空心水煎，或单苍朮膏。水泄少食者，升阳益胃汤。不泄少食者，二陈汤加白朮、黄芪、童便、制香附、当归、芍药、牡丹皮、麦门冬、山楂、麦芽。因饮食积者，更加莪朮、枳壳。　　湿痰占住血海地位经闭者，导痰汤加川芎、黄连。不可服地黄，泥膈故也。如用须姜汁炒过。丹溪之言，洵不可易。[53p]

When one suffers from cold due to eating cold food or being exposed to dampness, leading to the stagnation of blood, one should use Wujisan with Mahuang, Mudanpi, and Honghua. If emotional stress causes Qi stagnation, use Fenxin Qiyin with Qianghuo, Banxia, Sangpi, Qingpi, and add Chuanxiong, Dangui, Xiangfu, Ezhul, and Yanhusuo. If there is heat present, add Huangqin or use a minor modulation formula with Xiangfu pill.

For cases of abundant Qi and blood, when the meridians are obstructed, or phlegm is present, one can use Dan Dahuang Gao. Alternatively, juice from Verbena can be boiled down to a pill or roasted until charred. Decoction of Honghua and Danggui can be taken.

For internal injuries from diet, overexertion, or weakness of the spleen and stomach, wherein one feels fatigue, has fever, abdominal pain, and reduced appetite without producing blood, one should take Buzhong Yiqi Decoction with Chuanxiong, Shengdihuang, and Tianhuafen. If there is abdominal rumbling and absence of menstruation, the issue is in the stomach, which is weak and cannot produce Qi and blood; in that case, one should use Houpo (five qian), boiled with water on an empty stomach, or just take a decoction of Cangzhu.

For diarrhea with reduced appetite, use Shengyang Yiqi Decoction. If there is no diarrhea and still reduced appetite, use Erchen Decoction with Baizhu, Huangqi, Tongbian, Zhi Xiangfu, Danggui, Shaoyao, Mudanpi, Maidong, Hawthorn, and Malt. For issues related to food stagnation, add Ezhul and Zhike.

If damp phlegm occupies the blood sea and causes menstrual obstruction, use Dantang Decoction with Chuanxiong and Huanglian. Do not consume Dihuang as it clogs the diaphragm; if used, ginger juice should be stir-fried. Indeed, the words of Danxi should not be taken lightly.[53p]

　　胃热消渴，善食渐瘦，津液为热燥，渴者，宜泻胃热，四物汤合调胃承气汤，名玉烛散；再台凉膈散，名三和散。轻者小柴胡汤合四物汤，去人参、半夏加天花粉。素虚形瘦、口燥，善食厚味，郁为痰火。有潮热者，逍遥散加黄芩无薄荷，或四物汤加桃仁、红花，或加味养荣丸亦可。　　大概经水不通，肥人多气弱有湿痰、瘦人多血怯有火。　　少年大脱血，或醉后入房，气竭肝伤，月事衰少者，其治法已见《内经》腹中论篇。[54p]

Heat in the stomach causes thirst, and those who eat well may gradually lose weight. When fluids are dried by heat, those who feel thirsty should clear the heat from the stomach. One can use a combination of Siwu Decoction and Tiaoge Chushi Decoction, called Yuzhu Powder; or alternatively, use the Liangge Powder, known as Sanhe Powder. For mild cases, a combination of Xiaochaihu Decoction and Siwu Decoction, removing ginseng and Banxia, and adding Tianhuafen is recommended.

Those with a thin physique, dry mouth, and a tendency to crave rich foods could have phlegm-fire due to stagnation. If there is a sensation of heat, one may use Xiaoyao Powder combined with Huangqin, without mint, or Siwu Decoction with Tao Ren and Honghua, or even add the nourishing Yangrong Pill.

Generally, the passage of water is blocked. Overweight individuals tend to have weak qi and damp phlegm, while thin individuals usually have a fear of blood and possess heat.

Young people may experience significant blood loss, or following drunkenness may engage in sexual relations, leading to depletion of qi and damage to the liver, especially if menstrual flow decreases. Treatment methods for these conditions can be found in the "Neijing," specifically in the section on abdominal discussions.[54p]

　　堕胎及多产育伤血，或误服汗下克伐之药，以致血衰气乏不行者，十全大补汤。　　经虽来或血渐少而后不通，皆堕胎及产多者，谓之血枯。原因心事不足，以致脾不磨食，故肺金失养而气滞不行，肾水不旺而血益日枯。初时参前参后，淋沥无时；脾胃衰甚，变为溏泄身肿；失治甚为症瘕痨瘵。　　总而言之，经水不通，不出虚热痰气四证，不调亦大相同。随证调治，饮食调和，自然血气流通；更有凝滞，然后可用红花当归散，紫葳散、通经丸、导经丸之类。虚者只用当归散以通之，通后又须养血益阴，使津液流通。苟不务气血充和，而惟以毒药攻逼，必死而已。
　　　　　经水不调[55p]

Miscarriage and excessive childbirth harm the blood, or mistakenly taking medicines that induce sweating and purging may lead to diminished blood flow and lack of energy. In such cases, use the Shiquan Dabu decoction.

If menstruation becomes irregular, with diminishing blood flow leading to stagnation, this is referred to as "blood desiccation." The root cause is insufficient emotional balance, which prevents the spleen from properly digesting food, causing a deficiency in lung nourishment and stagnant energy. Additionally, the kidneys' water element becomes deficient, leading to further depletion of blood over time. Initially, symptoms may include intermittent dripping; if the spleen and stomach become significantly weakened, it may develop into diarrhea and bodily swelling. If left untreated, this can lead to serious conditions such as abdominal masses and tuberculosis.

In summary, if menstruation is obstructed, without the presence of excessive heat, phlegm, or qi stagnation, the situation is generally similar. Adjust treatments according to the symptoms and harmonize diet to ensure the smooth flow of blood and energy. If there is significant stagnation, remedies such as Honghua Danggui powder, Ziqi powder, Tongjing pills, or Daojing pills may be used. For those with deficiencies, simply using Danggui powder to promote circulation is essential; afterward, it is necessary to nourish the blood and enhance yin to ensure fluid circulation. If one neglects to nourish qi and blood, relying solely on toxic medications for forceful treatment will certainly lead to death.[55p]

　　以期言之，对期者，性和血足易受孕，只差一二日者，亦不为害。　　以色言之，心主血，阴从阳，故以色红为正，虽不对期而色正者易调。　　后期三五日者，为血虚，四物汤加参、芪、白朮、陈皮、升麻。瘦人只是血少，四物汤倍当归、地黄，少加桃仁、红花。肥人多痰，二陈汤加南星、苍朮、滑石、芎、归、香附。　　来少色和者，四物汤。点滴欲闭，潮烦脉数者，四物汤去芎、地，如泽兰叶三倍、甘草少许，十味香附丸。内寒血濇，来少或日少，五六日以上者，四物汤加桃仁、红花、牡丹皮、葵花。　　先期三五日者，为血热，四物汤加芩、连；肥人加痰药。先十数日者，血气俱热也，四物汤加黄芩、柴胡、香附；肥人清海苍莎丸加黄连、白朮。　　来多或日多，五六日以上者，内热血散也，四物加芩、朮。瘦人有火者，固经丸。肥人多痰者，清海苍莎丸。　　或前或后，或多或少。或逾月不至，或一月再至，当归散、调经散、单丹参散。[56p]

To speak of the expected period, those whose nature is harmonious and whose blood is sufficient can conceive easily; a difference of one or two days is not harmful. In terms of color, the heart governs blood, and the yin follows the yang; thus, red is the correct color. Even if not exactly on time, those with the correct color can easily adjust.

If the period is delayed by three to five days, it indicates blood deficiency. In this case, take Si Wu Decoction with added ginseng, astragalus, white atractylodes, dried tangerine peel, and bulblet. For thin individuals with merely low blood, double the amount of angelica and rehmannia in the Si Wu Decoction, adding a small amount of peach kernel and safflower. For those who are overweight and have a lot of phlegm, add south star, fragrant atractylodes, talc, chuanxiong, angelica, and cyperus to Er Chen Decoction.

For those who have a slight color and harmony, use Si Wu Decoction. If there is dripping wanting to stop, with irritability and rapid pulse, use Si Wu Decoction without chuanxiong and rehmannia; replace with three times the amount of eupatorium leaf and a little licorice, and take Ten Flavor Cyperus Pill. If there is internal cold and blood stagnation, with little flow or a shortened period lasting five to six days or more, use Si Wu Decoction with peach kernel, safflower, peony root, and sunflower.

If the period comes several days early, it indicates heat in the blood. Use Si Wu Decoction with added qin and lian; overweight people should add phlegm remedies. If it comes ten or more days early, both blood and qi are heated; use Si Wu Decoction with added yellow qin, bupleurum, and cyperus; for overweight individuals, add Qinghai Cangsha Pill with yellow lian and white atractylodes.

If the flow is abundant or lasts several days, five or six days or more indicates internal heat dispersing the blood; use Si Wu Decoction with qin and atractylodes. If thin individuals have fire, take Guo Jing Pill. For those who are overweight and have phlegm, take Qinghai Cangsha Pill.

Periods may come early or late, in large or small amounts; there may be a month’s delay, or it may recur in a month. In such cases, take Dong Gui San, Adjusting Menstrual Powder, or Dan Dan Shen San.[56p]

　　时行时止，淋沥不断，腹中作痛，乃寒热邪气客于胞中，留滞血海外疼也。如有积下利不定，有所去则愈。脐下逆气，上攻胸膈欲呕者，桃仁散；或用当归四钱、干漆三钱，蜜丸服。如腰脐腹痛者，牛膝散。或行或止，心痛者失笑散。经水适来适断，往来寒热者，先服小柴胡汤加地黄，后以四物汤和之。有月事频数者，四物汤倍芍药加黄芪。有经行不止者，四物汤加地榆、阿胶、荆芥。热者倍黄芪或吞固经丸。　　色紫者风也，黑者热甚也，淡白者虚也，或挟痰停水以混之也。[57p]

At times it flows, at times it stops, dripping continuously; pain arises in the abdomen, indicating that cold and heat evils are lodged in the body, causing pain due to stagnation of blood. If there are symptoms of intermittent diarrhea, healing occurs after excretion. If there is rebellious qi below the navel, attacking the chest and causing the urge to vomit, use Peach Kernel Powder; alternatively, take three qian of Danggui and three qian of Jangqi, formed into honey pills. For pain in the waist and abdomen, use Niu Xi Powder. If there is a change between movement and stillness, with heart pain, use Shixiao Powder. When the menstrual flow comes and stops appropriately, alternating between cold and heat, first take Xiao Chai Hu Decoction with added Di Huang, then harmonize with Si Wu Decoction. For frequent menstruation, increase the amount of Shao Yao in Si Wu Decoction and add Huang Qi. For continuous menstruation, add Di Yu, Ejiao, and Jing Jie to Si Wu Decoction. If hot, double the amount of Huang Qi or take Gu Jing Wan.

Purple discharge indicates wind, black indicates severe heat, pale white indicates deficiency, or it may be mixed with phlegm and stagnant water.[57p]

如烟尘水，如屋漏水，如豆汁，或带黄混浊模糊者，湿痰也。成块作片，色不变者，气滞也，或风冷乘之也。色变紫黑者，血热也。大概紫者，四物汤加防风、白芷、荆芥；黑者，四物汤加芩、连、香附；淡白者，古芎归汤加参、芪、白芍、香附；有痰者。二陈汤加芎、归；如烟尘者，二陈汤加秦艽、防风、苍朮；如豆汁者，四物汤加芩、连；成块者，四物汤加香附、延胡索、枳壳、陈皮。通用琥珀调经丸、百子附归丸、墨附丸。　　月水循环，纤疴不作，乃能有子。若兼潮疼，重则加之咳血汗呕，或泻有潮汗，则血愈消耗。[58p]

Like smoke and dust, like leaking water from a roof, like the color of bean juice, or mixed with yellow and muddy, this signifies damp phlegm. If it forms lumps or pieces and the color remains unchanged, it indicates qi stagnation, possibly due to wind-cold invasion. If the color changes to purple or black, this indicates heat in the blood. Generally, for purple, use Si Wu Tang with Fang Feng, Bai Shi, and Jing Jie; for black, Si Wu Tang with Qín, Lián, and Xiang Fu; for pale white, use Guo Qiong Gui Tang with Ren Shen, Qi, Bai Shao, and Xiang Fu; if there is phlegm, use Er Chen Tang with Qiong and Gui; if like smoke and dust, use Er Chen Tang with Qin Jiao, Fang Feng, and Cang Zhu; if like bean juice, use Si Wu Tang with Qín and Lián; if it forms lumps, use Si Wu Tang with Xiang Fu, Yan Hu Suo, Zhi Ke, and Chen Pi. Commonly used remedies include Hu Po Tiao Jing Wan, Bai Zi Fu Gui Wan, and Mo Fu Wan. The menstrual cycle should proceed normally; only then can one have offspring. If accompanied by tidal pain which intensifies with coughing blood, sweating, vomiting, or diarrhea with tidal sweat, then the blood will be further depleted.[58p]

有效呕则气往上行，泻则津偏于后，疼则疾结于中，是以必先去病而后可以滋血调经。就中潮热疼痛，尤为妇女常病。盖血滞积入骨髓，便为骨蒸；血滞积瘀于中，与日生新血相搏，则为疼痛；血枯不能滋养百骸，则蒸热于外；血枯包络火盛，或挟痰气食积，寒冷外邪，则为疼痛。　　潮热有时，为内伤，为虚；无时，为外感，为实。虚者大温经汤，热者四物汤加柴、芩，经闭者滋血汤，骨蒸者大胡连丸、大乌鸡丸。五心潮者，四物汤加黄连、胡黄连。无汗者，茯苓补心汤。[59p]

When there is effective vomiting, the energy rises; when there is diarrhea, the essence flows to the back; when there is pain, it is a sudden obstruction in the middle. Therefore, one must first eliminate the illness before nourishing the blood and regulating the menstrual cycle. Among the conditions of tidal fever and pain, these are particularly common among women.
